Exclusivity of Necessary Existence to Allah
Commentary refutes attributing necessary existence to attributes and defines al-uluhiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why necessary existence cannot be attributed to Allah's attributes and what the correct definition of divinity (al-uluhiyya) entails.

Core Idea
Necessary existence belongs to Allah alone; attributes are possible in themselves.

This passage tackles a subtle theological debate: Are Allah's attributes also necessary in existence? Some scholars argued that since attributes are inseparable from Allah's essence, they too must be necessary. The commentator firmly rejects this, explaining why it contradicts tawhid, and then provides the correct definition of divinity based on self-sufficiency and dependence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the two positions mentioned: al-Sa'd's view and Hamid al-Darir's view. Pay attention to the commentator's rejection.
The commentator refers to a later refutation of al-Sa'd's view.
2
Understand the refutation
The commentator says that attributing essential necessary existence to attributes contradicts tawhid. Al-Sa'd's attempt to make them necessary for the essence but possible in themselves is rejected.
This shows the strict monotheism of Sunni kalam.
3
Learn the correct definition of al-uluhiyya
Divinity means deservingness of worship, which is expressed by Allah's self-sufficiency and the dependence of all others. This is the verified position.
The commentator warns to hold fast to this truth and not to know truth by men.

This passage deals with the debated issue of whether the attribute of necessary existence (wujub al-wujud) applies exclusively to Allah or also to His attributes. The Essential Attribute Defined
Ithaaf al-Mureed defines the essential attribute with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the essential attribute (al-sifa al-nafsiyya) and how it differs from other divine attributes.

Core Idea
The essential attribute is the essence itself, not an extra quality.

In Ash'ari theology, attributes of Allah are divided into categories. The first and most fundamental is the essential attribute (al-sifa al-nafsiyya). This short passage from Ithaaf al-Mureed defines it precisely and gives simple examples. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping the rest of the attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text carefully, noticing the key terms. Then read the literal translation to grasp the basic meaning.
2
Understand the definition
The passage defines the essential attribute as a positive attribute that indicates the essence itself without any additional meaning. Think about what 'without additional meaning' means.
3
Examine the examples
The examples given are 'the substance being a substance,' 'being an essence,' 'being a thing,' and 'being existent.' These are not separate attributes; they are the essence itself. Try to see why.
4
Contrast with other attributes
This concept helps distinguish attributes that are identical to the essence from those that are additional (like knowledge, power). Reflect on the difference.
This will be expanded in later lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الأول: الصفة النفسية [ تعريف الصفة النفسية ] والمراد بالصّفة النّفسيَّة: صفةٌ ثبوتيَّةٌ تدل على نفس الذات دون معنى زائد عليها (١) ، ككون الجوهر جوهرا (۲) ، وذاتا ، وشيئا ، وموجود (۳).
The first section: The essential attribute. [Definition of the essential attribute] And by 'essential attribute' is meant: a positive attribute that indicates the essence itself without an additional meaning, such as the substance being a substance, and an essence, and a thing, and existing.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage defines the essential attribute (al-sifa al-nafsiyya). It is a positive attribute (sifa thubutiyya) that indicates the essence itself without any additional meaning (dun ma'na za'id 'alayha). Examples are given: the substance being a substance, being an essence, being a thing, and being existent. These are not separate attributes; they are the essence itself. This concept is fundamental in Ash'ari theology to distinguish between attributes that are identical to the essence and those that are additional (as in the case of the attributes of knowledge, power, etc.).

Key Takeaway

The Debate on Existence: Identity or Addition?
Ithaaf al-Mureed explains two positions on existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main positions on whether existence is identical to the essence or additional to it, and the implications for divine attributes.

Core Idea
Existence: is it the same as the essence or something extra?

This passage introduces a foundational debate in kalam: is existence (wujud) identical to the essence of a thing, or is it an additional attribute? The answer shapes how we understand divine attributes and the very nature of reality. Let's explore the two contrasting views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three matters
The passage opens by stating three things to explain about existence. Read the first few lines to identify them.
The third matter is only mentioned; the passage focuses on the first matter.
2
Compare the two views
Find where al-Ash'ari's view is stated and where al-Razi's view is stated. Note the key difference: is existence ayn al-dhat or za'id?
3
Understand 'hal' (state)
In al-Razi's view, existence is a 'hal' intermediate between existent and non-existent. Grasp what this means.
This introduces a third category beyond simply existent/non-existent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القول في الوجود يحتاج إلى بيان ثلاثة أمور: الأول: معنى الوجود، والثاني: معنى وجوبه له سبحانه، والثالث: الدليل على وجوب وجود الله تعالى. فأما الكلام على الأول فيستدعي أن نُقدّم لك بحثًا يترتب عليه بيان معنى الوجود، وهذا البحث يتلخص في أنَّ الوجود مطلقا ـ نعني سواء أكان صفةٌ للقديم أم كان صفة للحادث - هل هو عين الذات الموجودة أو هو غير الذات ؟ وقد اختلف العلماء في هذه المسألة، فذهب أبو الحسن الأشعري : إلى أن الوجود هو نفس الذات، وعلى هذا لا يقال إن الوجود صفة، لأن الصفة اسم للأمر الزائد على الموصوف، وعلى هذا يكون عد المتكلمين والمؤلفين المصنف والشارح الوجود من الصفات الواجبة له سبحانه مشتملا على شيء من التّسامح، وسببه : أنهم رأوا أنه يصح وصف ذات الله تعالى لفظاً بما يُشتق من الوجود، فيقال: «ذات الله موجودة» فلما رأوا أنَّ الوجود يكون وصفًا في اللفظ كالصفة الحقيقية في نحو قولنا: الله تعالى عالم وقادر أطلقوا لفظ الصفة على الوجود تشبيها له بها وقال قوم منهم الرَّازِيُّ : الوجود أمر زائد على الذات، على معنى أنه صفة ثابتة في الخارج لكنها لم تصل إلى درجة الموجودات التي تشاهد وتحسُّ ، فهي واسطة بين الموجود الخارجي والمعدوم، وهذا الفريق أثبت واسطة بين الموجود والمعدوم، وسمّي هذه الواسطة عنده ثلاثة: معدوم، وموجود ، وحالٌ . أما الفريق الأول فليس عنده إلا قسمان: الموجود والمعدوم. وقد استدل القائلون بأن الوجود عين الموجود بحجج كثيرة نجتزئ لك منها بدليلين:
The discussion on existence requires explaining three matters: First: the meaning of existence, Second: the meaning of its necessity for Him, exalted, Third: the proof for the necessity of the existence of God, exalted. As for the speech on the first, it requires that we present to you a discussion that results in clarifying the meaning of existence. This discussion is summarised in that existence absolutely - meaning whether it is an attribute of the eternal or an attribute of the temporal - is it identical to the existent essence or is it other than the essence? The scholars have differed on this issue. Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari held that existence is the essence itself. On this basis, existence is not called an attribute, because an attribute is a name for something additional to the described. On this basis, the counting of existence by the theologians and authors, the commentator, as one of the attributes necessary for Him, exalted, includes some tolerance. Its reason is: they saw that it is correct to describe the essence of God verbally with what is derived from existence, so it is said: 'the essence of God is existent.' When they saw that existence is a description in wording like a real attribute in our saying 'God, exalted, is knowing and powerful', they applied the term 'attribute' to existence by analogy to it. And a group, among them al-Razi, said: existence is additional to the essence, meaning that it is an attribute established in external reality but it does not reach the level of observable and sensible existents, so it is an intermediate between external existent and non-existent. This group affirmed an intermediate between existent and non-existent, and called this intermediate three: non-existent, existent, and state. As for the first group, they have only two categories: existent and non-existent. And those who say existence is identical to the existent have argued with many proofs, from which we will present to you two proofs:
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage discusses the nature of existence (wujud). It first outlines three issues to be addressed: the meaning of existence, the meaning of its necessity for God, and the proof for the necessity of God's existence. It then focuses on the first issue: whether existence is identical to the essence or additional. It presents the view of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, who held that existence is identical to the essence (ayn al-dhat). On this view, existence is not a true attribute, because an attribute must be additional to the described. Nevertheless, theologians still call existence an attribute by way of verbal analogy, because it is similar in wording to real attributes like 'knowing' and 'powerful'. The second view, held by al-Razi and others, is that existence is additional to the essence (za'id 'ala al-dhat). It is a real attribute but not a full-fledged existent; rather, it is a 'state' (hal) intermediate between existence and non-existence. This group affirms three categories: existent, non-existent, and state, while the first group only has two. The passage concludes by mentioning that the proponents of the identity view have many proofs, of which two will be presented.

وجود
ذات
صفة
حال
موجود
معدوم
أبو الحسن الأشعري
الرازي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Ash'ari denies existence as an attribute altogether.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari denies existence as a real additional attribute, but he acknowledges that it is called an attribute verbally by analogy.

Checkpoint

A) Existence is additional to the essence.
B) Existence is identical to the essence.
C) Existence is a state (hal) between existence and non-existence.
D) Existence is a sensible existent.

Key Takeaway
The debate on the nature of existence is foundational for understanding divine attributes in kalam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

Refuting the Objection Against Existence as a Self-Attribute
Objection and refutation regarding existence as sifa nafsiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari school defends the view that existence is a self-attribute by clarifying that the essence apart from existence is not non-existent but neutral.

Core Idea
The possible essence is neither existent nor non-existent in itself.

This passage addresses a key objection to the Ash'ari concept of existence as a self-attribute (sifa nafsiyya). The objector claims that if existence is not an additional attribute, then considering the essence without existence makes it non-existent, leading to a contradiction when we say it is existent. The author provides a refutation by explaining the nature of possible quiddity (mahiyya).

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objector's argument carefully. Why does he think describing the essence as existent is contradictory? Note that he assumes the essence without existence is non-existent.
This is the key assumption that the author will challenge.
2
Identify the author's denial
The author says 'We do not concede that the essence is non-existent when it is a substrate for existence, suitable for it, empty of it.' This is the refutation's starting point.
3
Examine the example of the possible
The author uses the possible being (mumkin) to illustrate. A possible thing is neither necessarily existent nor necessarily non-existent; it is receptive to both. So its essence is empty of both descriptions.
The possible being is a clear counterexample to the objector's assumption.
4
Grasp the resolution
Therefore, the essence apart from existence is not non-existent; it is neutral. When existence comes to it, it becomes described by existence without contradiction.
This resolves the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الأول: الصفة النفسية حيث هي - أي: مع قطع النظر عن هذا الوجود - غير موجودة، على معنى أنها حينئذ تكون معروضة للوجود صالحة له خالية عنه، فتكون معدومة، فإذا قلت: «الذات موجودة» كنت قد وصفت المعدوم بالوجود وهذا تناقض. ويجاب عن هذا: أنا لا نسلم أن الذات إذا كانت معروضة للوجود صالحة له خالية عنه تكون معدومة؛ لأن الممكن مثلا: هو ما لا تقتضي ذاته أن يكون موجودا أو معدوما، فهو صالح لأن يتوارد عليه الوجود والعدم على سبيل البدل، فهو من حيث ذاته عار عنهما جميعا، نعني أن ماهيته في حد ذاتها خالية عنهما غير موصوفة بواحد منهما.
The first section: the sifa nafsiyya (self-attribute). Where it – i.e., disregarding this existence – is non-existent, meaning that at that time it is a substrate for existence, suitable for it, empty of it, so it is non-existent. So if you say: 'The essence is existent,' you have described the non-existent with existence, and this is a contradiction. And it is answered about this: We do not concede that the essence, when it is a substrate for existence, suitable for it, empty of it, is non-existent; because the possible, for example, is that whose essence does not necessitate that it be existent or non-existent, so it is suitable for existence and non-existence to alternate upon it, so in terms of its essence it is devoid of both, meaning that its quiddity in itself is empty of both, not described by either.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer regarding the Ash'ari view that existence is a sifa nafsiyya (self-attribute) that is not additional to the essence. The objector argues: if existence is not additional, then when we consider the essence without existence, it is non-existent; therefore, saying 'the essence is existent' would be describing a non-existent as existent, which is contradictory. The author refutes this by denying that the essence when considered as a substrate for existence is non-existent. He uses the example of the possible being: a possible thing does not necessitate existence or non-existence in itself; it is equally receptive to both. Therefore, its essence apart from existence is not non-existent but rather neutral, devoid of both descriptions. Thus, describing it with existence when existence occurs is not contradictory because the essence was not actually non-existent prior to existence; it was merely not described by existence.

Key Terms
صفة نفسية (sifa nafsiyya)
وجود (wujud)
ذات (dhat)
ممكن (mumkin)
ماهية (mahiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The essence apart from existence is non-existent (absolute nothingness).
Correction: The essence apart from existence is not non-existent but rather neutral, devoid of both existence and non-existence, like the possible quiddity.

Checkpoint
According to the author's refutation, what is the status of the essence when it is considered apart from existence?
A) It is non-existent.
B) It is existent.
C) It is devoid of both existence and non-existence.
D) It is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari defense of existence as a self-attribute relies on the concept that the essence is neutral, not non-existent, prior to existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are a possible being – your essence did not necessitate your existence. If your very quiddity was neutral, not non-existent, then what does your current existence demand of you? How will you live today as one who was chosen from neutrality to exist?
?
The objector thought that describing what is neutral as existent was contradictory. Do you ever feel you are 'not yet' what you should be? Does knowing that your potential is real – not nothing – give you the courage to act? What will you do this week to actualize that potential?
?
If Allah describes a possible being as existent after He creates it, and this is not a contradiction, then His speech about your future actions is truthful. Are you living as if your deeds are already known? How will you align your choices with what Allah has inscribed?

Second Proof and Its Refutation: Reality vs. Description
Ibn Jawhara presents a syllogistic proof for the addition of existence to essence and its refutation via the reality-description distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the claim that existence is additional to the essence is argued via a second-figure syllogism and why the author refutes it by distinguishing between knowledge of reality and knowledge of description.

Core Idea
Knowing a thing by its description is not knowing its reality.

In this passage, Ibn Jawhara presents one of the proofs used by those who argue that existence is an additional attribute: a syllogism based on our knowledge of God's existence versus our ignorance of His essence. The author refutes it by challenging whether we truly know existence 'as a reality' or only as a description. This is a subtle but crucial distinction in kalām.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof carefully
Identify the two premises: (1) God's essence is unknown, (2) God's existence is known. Then see how they form a second-figure syllogism leading to the conclusion: essence ≠ existence.
Notice that 'unknown' and 'known' are different predicates, which is key to the syllogism.
2
Understand the author's refutation
The author denies the major premise that existence is known. He distinguishes between knowing the reality (haqiqah) and knowing via description (wasf).
The reality of existence is just as unknown as the reality of the essence.
3
Grasp the implication
If existence is only known by description (e.g., eternal), then the syllogism's premise is not about the same 'existence' the conclusion requires.
This refutation protects the doctrine that existence is identical to essence.
4
Apply the distinction
Realize that this distinction applies broadly in theology: we often know attributes only by their descriptions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد استدل القائلون بأن الوجود أمر زائد على الذات بأدلة نذكر لك منها واحدا، لتعرف مهيع البحث. قالوا: إن ذاته تعالى غير معلومة لنا، وإن وجوده سبحانه معلوم لنا، وهذا قياس من الشكل الثاني ونتيجته: إن ذاته تعالى غير وجوده. ويجاب عن هذا الدليل: بأنا لا نسلم إطلاق قولكم: إن وجوده تعالى معلوم لنا لأن حقيقة الوجود غير معلومة لنا، كما أن حقيقة الذات غير معلومة لنا، وإنما المعلوم لنا: الوجود من حيث الوصف، وهو أن ذلك الوجود لا يسبقه عدم، ولا يلحقه عدم، ولو قلنا: إن ذاته أيضا معلومة لنا من حيث الوصف؛ ككونها لا تشبه شيئا ولا يشبهها شيء كان صحيحا أيضا.
And those who say that existence is additional to the essence have adduced proofs; we will mention one of them for you, so that you may know the path of inquiry. They said: His essence (Exalted is He) is unknown to us, and His existence (Glorified is He) is known to us, and this is a second-figure syllogism, and its conclusion is: His essence (Exalted is He) is other than His existence. And this proof is answered: We do not concede your unqualified statement that His existence (Exalted is He) is known to us, because the reality of existence is unknown to us, just as the reality of the essence is unknown to us; rather, what is known to us is existence in terms of description, namely that that existence is not preceded by non-existence and is not followed by non-existence. And if we said that His essence is also known to us in terms of description, such as that it does not resemble anything and nothing resembles it, that would also be correct.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage presents a proof and its refutation. The proof is an argument from those who claim existence is additional to the essence. They reason: God's essence is unknown to us, but His existence is known to us; therefore, by a second-figure syllogism, His essence is not identical to His existence. The author refutes this by denying the major premise that existence is known. He argues that the reality (haqiqa) of existence is unknown to us, just as the reality of the essence is unknown. What is known is existence only in terms of its descriptive attribute (min haythu al-wasf), i.e., that it is eternal, not preceded or followed by non-existence. Similarly, the essence is also known only in terms of description (e.g., that it is incomparable). Thus, the proof fails because it assumes knowledge of the reality of existence, which we do not have.

Key Terms
زائد على الذات
قياس الشكل الثاني
حقيقة الوجود
وصف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'known' in the proof refers to comprehensive knowledge of the reality of existence.
Correction: The author clarifies that we only know existence by its description (eternality), not its reality (haqiqa).

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the claim that God's existence is known to us?
A) Because God's existence is unknowable.
B) Because only the description of existence is known, not its reality.
C) Because existence is identical to the essence.
D) Because the syllogism is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between knowing a thing by its reality and knowing it by its description is crucial for correct theological reasoning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often say you 'know' God exists. But do you confuse that descriptive knowledge with truly comprehending His reality? How does this lesson confront your assumption that you can fully grasp His essence?
?
When you describe God as 'eternal' or 'incomparable,' do you stop at the word, or do you let the fact that these are only descriptions humble your heart? What would change in your worship if you truly admitted you cannot encompass His reality?
?
You rely on logical proofs for God's existence and attributes. But this lesson shows that even a seemingly sound syllogism can fail if its terms are equivocal. How many of your own certainties about God are actually built on unexamined assumptions? Will you now revisit them with the same critical spirit?

Philosophical and Karramiyya Views on Existence
Reports the philosophers' and Karramiyya's views and notes their rebuttal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' and Karramiyya's positions on existence and why the author finds them problematic.

Core Idea
Other sects defined existence in ways that the Ash'aris reject.

Before diving into the Ash'ari definition, it is helpful to see what other groups said about existence. The philosophers claimed that existence is identical to God's essence, while the Karramiyya treated it as an attribute of meaning. The author briefly mentions these views and signals that they are easily refuted.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on philosophers
Read the Arabic sentence about the philosophers' view carefully. Notice their reasoning: because God is one, existence cannot be other than Him.
The philosophers distinguish between originated and eternal existence.
2
Read the Karramiyya view
The Karramiyya say existence is an attribute of meaning, like power and will. Compare this to the philosophers' view.
3
Consider the author's response
The author states 'Its rebuttal is not hidden.' Think about why this view might be problematic from an Ash'ari perspective.
The author does not elaborate, but the student should reflect on the implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا، وقد قالت الفلاسفة: إن الوجود غير الموجود في الحادث، وأما في القديم فوجوده عينه، لأنه تعالى واجب الوجود وهو واحد من كل وجه، فلو كان وجوده غيره لتكثر، لأن الموصوف يتكثر عندهم بكثرة الصفات، وذلك يؤدي إلى التركيب المؤدي إلى الإمكان، وهو مناف للوجوب، ورد ذلك غير خاف. وقالت الكرامية: الوجود صفة معنى كالقدرة والإرادة. إذا علمت ذلك فاعلم أن الأشاعرة يعرفون الوجود بأنه: «صفة نفسية يدل الوصف بها على الذات دون معنى زائد عليها»، وقد يقال: «الوجود صفة تصحح لموصوفها أن يرى»، وهذا هو الذي ذكره الشارح الله، وقد علمت أن تعبيرهم عن الوجود بأنه صفة على مذهب الأشعري فيه تسامح، والمراد أنه تجوز حيث شبهوا الوجود بالصفة الحقيقية كالعلم، بجامع أن كلا منهما يقع صفة في اللفظ، فيقال: «ذات الله موجودة» كما يقال: «الله عالم»، واستعاروا اسم المشبه به وهو لفظ صفة للمشبه، ففيه على هذا التقرير استعارة تصريحية.
Now, the philosophers have said that existence is other than the existent in the originated, but in the Eternal His existence is identical to Him, because He (Exalted) is Necessary of Existence and is one from every aspect, so if His existence were other than Him, multiplicity would occur, because the described becomes multiple according to them by multiplicity of attributes, and that leads to composition leading to contingency, which contradicts necessity. Its rebuttal is not hidden. And the Karramiyya said: Existence is an attribute of meaning like power and will. When you know that, then know that the Ash'aris define existence as: 'A self-attribute (sifa nafsiyya) whose description indicates the essence without an additional meaning upon it.' And it is also said: 'Existence is an attribute that makes it valid for its described to be seen.' This is what the commentator (Allah) mentioned. And you have known that their expression of existence as an attribute in the school of Ash'ari involves lenience; the intended meaning is metaphor (tajawwuz) as they likened existence to a real attribute (al-sifa al-haqiqiyya) such as knowledge, with the common factor that each occurs as a predicate in language, so it is said: 'The essence of God is existent' just as it is said: 'God is knowing.' And they borrowed the name of the compared-to (al-mushabbah bihi), which is the word 'attribute,' for the compared (al-mushabbah); so in this explanation it is a manifest metaphor (isti'ara tasrihiyya).
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage covers several views and the Ash'ari definition. First, the philosophers hold that in originated things, existence is other than the existing essence, but in God (the Eternal) existence is identical to His essence because He is wajib al-wujud (Necessary of Existence) and absolutely one; otherwise, composition and contingency would arise. The author notes this is easily refuted. Then the Karramiyya say existence is a 'sifat ma'na' (attribute of meaning) like power or will. Next, the author presents the Ash'ari definition: existence is a sifa nafsiyya (self-attribute) indicating the essence without an additional meaning. Another definition is that it makes the described valid to be seen. The author then comments that calling existence an 'attribute' in Ash'ari doctrine is lenient (tasamuh); it is metaphorical because they likened it to real attributes like knowledge, sharing the common factor that both function as linguistic predicates. This borrowing is identified as an explicit metaphor (isti'ara tasrihiyya), where they borrowed the term 'attribute' (the compared-to) for existence (the compared).

Key Terms
وجود
واجب الوجود
صفة معنى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers, why must God's existence be identical to His essence?
A) Because existence is an attribute of meaning.
B) Because He is Necessary of Existence and absolutely one.
C) Because the Karramiyya said so.
D) Because existence is other than the existent in the originated.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers and Karramiyya held views on existence that the Ash'aris consider flawed, setting the stage for the Ash'ari definition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever unconsciously imagine God as having 'parts' because you think of His attributes separately? How does the philosophers' argument against composition expose a hidden shirk in your perception of God's oneness?
?
The Karramiyya treated existence as just another attribute like power. In your daily life, do you reduce your awareness of God's existence to just one aspect among many, forgetting that His existence is the foundation of all other attributes?
?
If you truly believed that God's existence is identical to His essence, how would it change the way you approach Him in worship—would you be more aware of His absolute simplicity or more cautious about how you describe Him?

Ash'ari Definition of Existence as Metaphor
Presents the Ash'ari definition of existence and explains its metaphorical use.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari definition of existence as a self-attribute and why calling it an 'attribute' is metaphorical.

Core Idea
Existence is not a real attribute but a linguistic metaphor.

Having seen other views, we now turn to the Ash'ari definition. Existence is defined as a 'self-attribute' that merely indicates the essence without adding anything. The author then clarifies that calling existence an 'attribute' is a metaphor, not a literal description.

Guided Path
1
Read the Ash'ari definition
Read the Arabic definition carefully: existence is a self-attribute (sifa nafsiyya) that indicates the essence without additional meaning.
This distinguishes it from real attributes like knowledge.
2
Read the second definition
Another definition: existence makes the described valid to be seen. Consider how this relates to the first.
3
Understand the metaphor
The author explains that calling existence an 'attribute' is metaphorical. They likened it to real attributes because both function as linguistic predicates.
This is an explicit metaphor (isti'ara tasrihiyya).

Source Text

Now, the philosophers have said that existence is other than the existent in the originated, but in the Eternal His existence is identical to Him, because He (Exalted) is Necessary of Existence and is one from every aspect, so if His existence were other than Him, multiplicity would occur, because the described becomes multiple according to them by multiplicity of attributes, and that leads to composition leading to contingency, which contradicts necessity. And they borrowed the name of the compared-to (al-mushabbah bihi), which is the word 'attribute,' for the compared (al-mushabbah); so in this explanation it is a manifest metaphor (isti'ara tasrihiyya).

This passage covers several views and the Ash'ari definition. Al-Razi's Definition of Existence
Al-Razi defines existence as a necessary uncaused state of the essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's definition of existence as a 'state' and how it excludes other types of attributes through its precise phrasing.

Core Idea
Existence is a state inseparable from the essence, not caused by any cause.

Al-Razi offers a precise definition of existence that distinguishes it from other attributes. The definition is built around the concept of a 'hal' (state) that necessarily belongs to the essence for its entire duration, uncaused. Understanding this definition clarifies how existence relates to the essence and what it is not.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read al-Razi's definition: 'The state necessarily belonging to the essence as long as the essence is not caused by a cause.' Notice the three key components: 'state,' 'necessarily belonging,' and 'not caused.'
The Arabic uses 'hal' which is a technical term.
2
Analyze each part
Examine the explanation of each phrase: 'necessarily belonging' means inseparable; 'as long as the essence' means for the entire duration; 'not caused' rules out any external cause. See how these components exclude attributes of meanings and negative attributes.
3
Understand the exclusions
The definition excludes attributes of meanings (sifat al-ma'ani) because they are not states; negative attributes (sifat salbiyya) are also excluded. Entitative attributes (sifat ma'nawiyya) are excluded either by the 'as long as' clause or the 'not caused' clause.
The exclusion of entitative attributes is twofold: either because their permanence depends on the permanence of their meanings, or because they are caused.
4
Reflect on the terminology
Note that calling something a 'hal' is a terminological choice. There is no dispute over terms; what matters is the conceptual distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والرازي ومن ينحو نحوه يعرف الوجود بأنه: «الحال الواجب للذات ما دامت الذات غير معللة بعلة». ومعنى قولهم الواجب للذات: الثابت لها ثبوتا لا ينفك عنها. و«ما» في قولهم: «ما دامت الذات» مصدرية ظرفية، أي: مدة دوام الذات، و«دام» تامة، وأظهروا الفاعل في قولهم: «ما دامت الذات» دفعا لما يتوهم عند إضماره من عود الضمير على الحال. وفائدة قولهم: «ما دامت الذات» التنبيه على أن الذات ملزومة للوجود، فمتى تحققت الذات تحقق وجودها. وقولهم: «غير معللة» هو بنصب «غير» على أنه حال من «الحال»، ولا يصح جعل «دام» ناقصة وجعل «غير» خبرها؛ لأن الذات لا تعلل. وقولهم: «الحال» يخرج عنه صفات المعاني والصفات السلبية، لأنها ليست بحال عندهم، وهو مجرد اصطلاح، ولا مشاحة فيه. وتخرج الصفات المعنوية إما بقولهم: «ما دامت الذات» لأن دوام الصفات المعنوية بدوام الذات معانيها لا بدوام الذات، وإما بقولهم: «غير معللة» لكون المعنوية تعلل بالمعاني، ألا ترى: أن القادر معلل بقيام القدرة بالذات، والمريد معلل بقيام الإرادة، وهلم جرا. بعد، فاعلم أن كثيرا من العلماء أجرى الخلاف بين الأشاعرة والرازي على ظاهره، وقال: إن معنى قول الأشعري: (إن الوجود عين الموجود) أنهما متحدان مفهوما ومصداقا، وعليه يجري كل ما تقدم ذكره، ومنه أن عدهم الوجود صفة يشتمل على التجوز الذي أوضحناه. ولكن جمعا من المحققين تأول هذه العبارة، وذهب إلى أن معنى كون الوجود عين الذات، أنه ليس له تحقق في الخارج زائدا على تحقق الذات، بل هو أمر اعتباري، فالمقصود أنه ليس للماهية من حيث هي تحقق ولعارضها المسمى بالوجود تحقق آخر، بحيث يكون هناك شيئان متحققان في الخارج كالجسم والبياض، وهذا لا ينافي كون الوجود أمرا اعتباريا يلاحظ في الذهن زيادة على ملاحظة الذات، وحينئذ يرجع قول الأشعري إلى قول الرازي، وعلى هذا لا يكون في عد الوجود صفة على مذهب الأشعري تسامح.
And al-Razi and those who follow his way define existence as: 'The state necessarily belonging to the essence as long as the essence is not caused by a cause.' And the meaning of their saying 'necessarily belonging to the essence' is: established for it with an establishment that does not separate from it. And 'ma' in their saying 'as long as the essence' is a verbal noun indicating time, i.e., the duration of the essence's permanence, and 'dam' is complete; and they made the agent explicit in 'as long as the essence' to prevent the misunderstanding that the pronoun would refer to the state if it were implicit. The benefit of their saying 'as long as the essence' is to alert that the essence is the necessary condition for existence, so whenever the essence is realized, its existence is realized. Their saying 'not caused by a cause' has 'ghayr' in the accusative as a circumstantial qualifier of 'state,' and it is not valid to make 'dam' incomplete and make 'ghayr' its predicate because the essence is not caused. Their saying 'state' excludes from it attributes of meanings and negative attributes, because they are not a state according to them, and this is mere terminology, and there is no dispute about it. The entitative attributes (sifat ma'nawiyya) are excluded either by their saying 'as long as the essence' because the permanence of entitative attributes is by the permanence of their meanings, not by the permanence of the essence, or by their saying 'not caused by a cause' because the entitative are caused by the meanings; do you not see that the powerful (al-qadir) is caused by the subsistence of power in the essence, and the willing (al-murid) is caused by the subsistence of will, and so on. Then know that many scholars took the disagreement between the Ash'aris and al-Razi at face value, and said: The meaning of Ash'ari's statement 'Existence is identical to the existent' is that they are united in concept and referent, and upon this everything mentioned previously proceeds, including that their counting existence as an attribute involves the metaphor we explained. But a group of verifiers (muhaqqiqun) interpreted this statement, and held that the meaning of 'existence is identical to the essence' is that it has no extra realization in the external beyond the realization of the essence; rather, it is a mental consideration (amr i'tibari). So what is intended is that the quiddity in itself has no realization, and its accident called existence does not have another realization, such that there would be two things realized externally like a body and whiteness. This does not contradict existence being a mental consideration observed in the mind in addition to the observation of the essence. In that case, Ash'ari's statement returns to al-Razi's statement, and on this there is no lenience in counting existence as an attribute in Ash'ari's school.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is an exposition and reconciliation. First, it presents al-Razi's definition of existence: it is a 'state' (hal) that necessarily belongs to the essence as long as the essence is not caused by a cause. This definition is then dissected: 'necessary' means it is inseparable; 'as long as the essence' uses 'as long as' as a temporal clause indicating the entire duration of the essence; 'not caused' rules out accidents. The definition excludes other types of attributes: attributes of meanings (sifat al-ma'ani, like power) are not states because they are caused; negative attributes (sifat salbiyya) are not states either. The entitative attributes (sifat ma'nawiyya, like being powerful) are excluded either because their permanence depends on the permanence of the meaning (e.g., power) or because they are caused. Then the author discusses the apparent disagreement between Ash'ari and Razi. One group takes it literally: Ash'ari meant existence and essence are identical in concept and referent, so his calling existence an attribute is metaphorical. But a group of verifiers (muhaqqiqun) interprets that Ash'ari meant existence has no extra external reality beyond the essence; it is a mental consideration (i'tibari). This interpretation aligns Ash'ari with Razi, removing the perceived lenience in calling existence an attribute.

Key Terms
الحال (hal)
الواجب للذات (al-wajib li al-dhat)
غير معللة (ghayr mu'allala)
صفات المعاني (sifat al-ma'ani)
صفات سلبية (sifat salbiyya)
صفات معنوية (sifat ma'nawiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Razi's definition, what does 'as long as the essence' (ma damat al-dhat) indicate?
A) Existence lasts only for a limited time.
B) Existence is dependent on a cause.
C) Existence accompanies the essence for its entire duration.
D) Existence is separate from the essence.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi defines existence as a necessary uncaused state that is inseparable from the essence, thereby distinguishing it from other attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How does al-Razi's claim that existence is an uncaused state inseparable from your essence confront the way you perceive your own existence as something you 'have' rather than something you 'are'? What would change in your daily life if you truly felt that your existence is not a possession but an unbreakable given from Allah?
?
The definition excludes attributes that are caused. Consider one area of your life where you feel your actions or identity are heavily caused by external factors—like your job, relationships, or reputation. If your very existence is uncaused and inseparable, how can this certainty give you courage to detach from those created causes and rely solely on the Creator?
?
Al-Razi's careful wording shows how a slight shift in definition can prevent serious theological errors. Reflect on one of your own beliefs about Allah or yourself that might be slightly off—a small nuance that, if corrected, could transform your worship. What would it take for you to seek and accept such a correction even if it is uncomfortable?

Reconciling Ash'ari and Razi on Existence
The author presents two interpretations of Ash'ari's statement and adopts the reconciliationist view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verifiers (muhaqqiqun) reconcile Ash'ari's statement that existence is identical to the existent with al-Razi's definition of existence as a mental consideration.

Core Idea
Ash'ari and Razi agree: existence has no extra external reality beyond the essence.

A superficial reading suggests Ash'ari and Razi disagree on whether existence is identical to the essence or a state. However, a group of verifiers offer an interpretation that harmonizes the two positions. They argue that Ash'ari's statement means existence is not a real extra entity in the external world, but a mental consideration (i'tibar), which aligns with Razi's definition.

Guided Path
1
Understand the apparent disagreement
Read how many scholars take the disagreement at face value: Ash'ari said existence is identical to the existent (concept and referent united), which leads to calling existence an attribute being metaphorical. This seems to contradict Razi's view that existence is a state.
2
Learn the verifiers' interpretation
The verifiers reinterpret Ash'ari's statement: existence is identical to the essence means it has no extra external realization beyond the essence. It is a mental consideration (amr i'tibari).
3
See how this reconciles with Razi
This interpretation makes Ash'ari's view return to al-Razi's view. Both agree that existence is not a real additional entity in the external world; the difference in terminology (state vs. mental consideration) is not substantive.
4
Evaluate the implication
Based on this reconciliation, counting existence as an attribute in Ash'ari's school is not a lenience but a technicality, since it is a mental attribute.

Two Interpretations of Ash'ari's Identity of Existence and Essence
Ash'ari's statement that existence is identical to the existent is interpreted literally and metaphorically.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two interpretations of al-Ash'ari's statement that existence is identical to the existent, and how the verifiers' metaphorical interpretation resolves the apparent conflict with al-Razi's view.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's identity of existence and essence can be read literally or as a mental consideration—resolving a key theological dispute.

This passage from a commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid dives into a classic controversy. Al-Ash'ari's famous phrase 'existence is identical to the existent' has been understood in two ways. The first is a straightforward identity in concept and reality; the second, favored by later verifiers, treats existence as a mental consideration with no extra-mental existence beyond the essence. Understanding these interpretations helps clarify the Ash'ari position on divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the literal English translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the two distinct interpretations introduced with 'but' (لٰكِنَّ).
2
Identify the two interpretations
Find the first interpretation (many scholars understand it literally) and the second (verifiers interpret it metaphorically). Note the key terms: 'مفهوما وماصدقا' for the literal, and 'أمر اعتباري' for the metaphorical.
3
Understand the reasoning behind the metaphorical interpretation
The verifiers argue that existence has no additional external realization beyond the essence; it is a mental consideration. This avoids having two things in the external world like body and whiteness.
This interpretation aligns al-Ash'ari with al-Razi's view, resolving the apparent disagreement.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this matters: it removes the need for figurative language in calling existence an attribute. The Ash'ari position is clarified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد، فاعلم أن كثيراً من العلماء أجرى الخلاف بين الأشاعرة والرازي على ظاهره، وقال: إن معنى قول الأشعري: (إن الوجود عين الموجود) أنهما متحدان مفهوما وماصدقا، وعليه يجري كل ما تقدم ذكره، ومنه أن عدهم الوجود صفة يشتمل على التجوز الذي أوضحناه، ولكن جمعا من المحققين تأول هذه العبارة، وذهب إلى أن معنى كون الوجود عين الذات، أنه ليس له تحقق في الخارج زائدا على تحقق الذات، بل هو أمر اعتباري، فالمقصود أنه ليس للماهية من حيث هي تحقق ولعارضها المسمى بالوجود تحقق آخر، بحيث يكون هناك شيئان متحققان في الخارج كالجسم والبياض، وهذا لا ينافي كون الوجود أمرا اعتباريا يلاحظ في الذهن زيادة على ملاحظة الذات، وحينئذ يرجع قول الأشعري إلى قول الرازي، وعلى هذا لا يكون في عد الوجود صفة على مذهب الأشعري تسامح.
Afterwards, know that many scholars understood the disagreement between the Ash'aris and al-Razi according to its apparent meaning, and said: The meaning of al-Ash'ari's statement 'Existence is identical to the existent' is that they are united both in conception (mafhūman) and in reference (māṣadaqan), and upon this proceeds everything mentioned previously, including that their counting existence as an attribute involves the figurative usage (al-tajawwuz) which we have clarified. But a group of verifiers (al-muḥaqqiqīn) interpreted this expression metaphorically, and held that the meaning of existence being identical to the essence is that it has no additional realization in the external world beyond the realization of the essence; rather, it is a mental consideration (amr iʿtibārī). So the intended meaning is that the quiddity (al-māhiyya) insofar as it is itself has no realization, and its accident called existence does not have another realization, such that there would be two things realized in the external world like a body and whiteness. This does not contradict that existence is a mental consideration observed in the mind in addition to the observation of the essence. In that case, al-Ash'ari's statement returns to al-Razi's statement, and upon this there is no laxity in counting existence as an attribute according to al-Ash'ari's school.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage discusses two interpretations of al-Ash'ari's famous statement that existence (al-wujud) is identical to the existent (al-mawjud). It is a refutation and clarification passage. The first interpretation is literal: many scholars take the disagreement between the Ash'aris and al-Razi at face value, meaning that existence and essence are identical both in concept and in reference. According to this view, counting existence as an attribute is a figurative usage, as previously explained. The second interpretation is offered by a group of verifiers (muhaqqiqun): they interpret al-Ash'ari's statement metaphorically. They hold that existence is not an extra thing in the external world over and above the essence; rather, it is a mental consideration. The quiddity (māhiyya) as such has no external realization, but its accident called existence is not a separate entity in the external world like whiteness is separate from a body. This does not contradict that existence is mentally considered in addition to the essence. According to this interpretation, al-Ash'ari's view converges with al-Razi's view, and there is no need for figurative language in calling existence an attribute. Thus, the apparent conflict is resolved.

Key Terms
الوجود
الموجود
عين
أمر اعتباري
الماهية
تحقق خارجي
تجوز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that al-Ash'ari's statement always implies an extra-mental distinction between existence and essence.
Correction: The verifiers show that it can be interpreted metaphorically: existence is a mental consideration, not a separate external entity.

Checkpoint
According to the verifiers (muhaqqiqun), what does it mean that existence is identical to the essence?
A) They are identical in concept and reference in the external world
B) Existence has no additional external realization beyond the essence
C) Existence is an attribute that subsists in the essence
D) Existence is a separate entity from the essence

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's statement can be interpreted either literally (identity in concept and reference) or metaphorically (existence as mental consideration), with the latter aligning with al-Razi's view.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How often do you assume that your initial understanding of a theological statement is the only correct one, even when deeper reflection might reveal a more nuanced meaning? Will you commit to seeking the muhaqqiqun's depth before settling on a view?
?
The muhaqqiqun resolved an apparent conflict by understanding existence as a mental consideration. In your own life, are there tensions or disagreements in matters of faith that you have simply accepted as irreconcilable, when a more careful distinction—like between real and mental—might bring harmony? What will you do to seek that resolution?
?
This lesson shows that a deep understanding can prevent the need for 'figurative language' in describing divine attributes. Are you content with superficial explanations of Allah's attributes, or will you strive to grasp the reality behind the words, even if it requires intellectual effort? What step will you take today to deepen that understanding?

The Three Types of Qidam and Its Nature
Enumerates three types of qidam and discusses a dispute over its nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three types of qidam and the theological disagreement about whether it is a positive or negative attribute.

Core Idea
Qidam is a negative attribute that simply denies non-existence.

This passage introduces qidam (eternity) as a key attribute of God. The author first distinguishes three kinds of qidam — essential, temporal, and relative — and then highlights a scholarly dispute over whether qidam is a positive essential attribute or a negative one. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping the traditional Islamic theological position on God's eternity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the literal translation. Notice the three types of qidam and the scholarly disagreement at the end.
The passage is incomplete but covers the main points.
2
Identify the three types of qidam
Find the three types: essential qidam (only for God), temporal qidam (lengthy duration, possible for creatures), and relative qidam (precedence in time). Understand why only essential qidam applies to God.
Temporal and relative qidam are impossible for God.
3
Understand the two aspects of investigation
The author says the study of qidam has two aspects: clarifying its meaning and proving it for God. Focus on the first aspect for now.
4
Grasp the scholarly positions
The passage outlines three views: qidam as an essential attribute, as a negative attribute, or as an attribute of meaning. Note that the preferred view is that it is a negative attribute.
This means qidam simply negates non-existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله: (والقِدَم ) (۱) شروعٌ في القسم الثاني من الصفات ـ أعني السَّلبيَّة (۱) اعلم أن القدم على ثلاثة أنواع: الأول: القدم الذاتي، وهو الثابت الله تعالى وسنفسره قريباً. والثاني: القدم الزماني، وهو مستحيل على الله تعالى ويُفسر بأنه: «طول مدة وجود الشيء» فإذا قلت: عُرجُون قديم، وضلال ،قديم، وبناء قديم، فالمعنى الذي تدل عليه هذه العبارة أنه قد طال عليه الزمان منذ وجد ، وذلك لا ينافي أنه حادث بمعنى كون وجوده مسبوقاً بالعدم، ومن هذا قوله جل ذكره: وَالْقَمَرَ قَدَّرْنَهُ مَنَازِلَ حَتَّى عَادَ كَالْعُرْجُونِ الْقَدِيمِ ﴾ [يس: ۳۹] وقوله تباركت أسماؤه: (تَاللهِ إِنَّكَ لَفِي ضَلَلِكَ الْقَدِيمِ ﴾ [يوسف: ٩٥ ] ، والثالث: القدم الإضافي، وهو أيضا محال على الله تعالى ويفسر بأنه: «سبقُ الشيء في الوجودِ لشيء آخر» وذلك كقدَمِ الأب بالنسبة للابن. ثم إن البحث في صفة القدم يتعلق بها من جهتين إحداهما : بيان معنى القدم، والثانية: إقامة الدليل على وجوب اتصافه بالقدم. والكلام عن الجهة الأولى يستدعي أنْ نُشير لك إلى خلاف بين أنْ نُشير لك إلى خلاف بين العلماء في صفة القدم ؛ أهي صفة نفسية كالوجود ؟ أم هي صفة سلبية كالمخالفة للحوادث؟ أم هي صفة المعاني كالعلم والقدرة ؟ فنقول : الراجح عند علماء الكلام أنَّ القدم صفةٌ سلبية ، ومعنى كونها سلبيةً أنها سلبتْ ونَفَتْ= صفات من
And His saying: 'and al-qidam (eternity)'—a commencement of the second category of attributes, namely the negative ones. Know that qidam is of three types: First: essential qidam (al-qidam al-dhati), which is established for God Almighty and we will explain it shortly. Second: temporal qidam (al-qidam al-zamani), which is impossible for God Almighty, and it is interpreted as 'the length of the duration of a thing's existence.' So if you say: 'an old palm stalk,' 'an old error,' 'an old building,' the meaning indicated by this expression is that time has been long upon it since it existed, and that does not contradict it being originated in the sense that its existence is preceded by non-existence. From this is His saying, may His mention be exalted: 'And the moon, We have determined for it phases until it returns like the old palm stalk' [Ya-Sin 39] and His saying, blessed be His names: 'By Allah, indeed you were in your old error' [Yusuf 95]. Third: relative qidam (al-qidam al-idafi), which is also impossible for God Almighty, and it is interpreted as 'the precedence of a thing in existence over another thing,' such as the qidam of a father relative to his son. Then, the investigation of the attribute of qidam pertains to it from two aspects: one is the clarification of the meaning of qidam, and the second is the establishment of the proof for the necessity of His being described with qidam. The discussion of the first aspect requires that we point out to you a disagreement among the scholars concerning the attribute of qidam: is it an essential attribute like existence? Or is it a negative attribute like being unlike originated things? Or is it an attribute of meanings like knowledge and power? We say: the preponderant view among the theologians (mutakallimun) is that qidam is a negative attribute, and the meaning of its being negative is that it negates and denies... attributes from...
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage introduces the attribute of qidam (eternity) as part of the negative attributes of God. It first distinguishes three types of qidam: essential qidam (only for God), temporal qidam (lengthy duration, possible for creatures, impossible for God), and relative qidam (precedence in time, also impossible for God). The author then notes that the investigation of qidam involves two aspects: its meaning and a proof that God has it. Regarding the first aspect, there is a disagreement among scholars: some consider it a positive essential attribute, others a negative attribute, and others a cognitive attribute. The author states that the preponderant view among mutakallimun is that qidam is a negative attribute, meaning it simply negates non-existence. The passage ends incompletely, but it sets up the discussion.

صفة سلبية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that temporal qidam (old age) is a form of eternity applicable to God.
Correction: Temporal qidam implies a beginning in time and is impossible for God; only essential qidam, which has no beginning, applies to Him.

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view, what kind of attribute is qidam?
A) Positive essential attribute
B) Negative attribute
C) Attribute of meaning
D) Relative attribute

Key Takeaway
The preponderant view is that qidam is a negative attribute, simply negating non-existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'God is eternal,' do you simply imagine He has existed for a very long time, or do you truly believe that non-existence is absolutely impossible for Him? How does the distinction between temporal qidam and essential qidam force you to purify your understanding of God's eternity? What will you change in how you speak about Him?
?
If qidam is only a negation of non-existence, not a positive addition, does that make God less perfect in your mind? Or does it unveil a perfection beyond adding qualities? How does this reshape your awe and love for a God whose very essence is free from any possibility of non-existence?
?
Consider something in your life you call 'old'—a building, a relationship, a habit. Now compare that to God's essential qidam. How does that comparison expose the gap between your reliance on temporal things and your need for the Eternal? What must you let go of to truly cling to al-Qadim alone?

The Three Types of Qidam (Pre-Eternity)
Classification of qidam into three types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three types of qidam (pre-eternity) and which apply to Allah.

Core Idea
Only essential qidam belongs to Allah; temporal and relative qidam are impossible for Him.

The author begins by classifying the term 'qidam' into three distinct meanings. Before we can discuss whether God is eternal, we must clarify what 'eternal' means. This passage provides that clarification, distinguishing the kind of eternity that belongs to Allah from other kinds that do not.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get an overview. Notice that the author lists three types of qidam and gives examples.
Pay attention to the Quranic verses cited for temporal qidam.
2
Identify the three types
Find the names of the three types: essential (dhati), temporal (zamani), and relative (idafi). Note which one is affirmed for Allah and which are negated.
3
Examine the examples
For temporal qidam, the author gives examples from the Quran: an old palm branch and an old error. For relative qidam, he gives the example of a father relative to his son. Understand why these are impossible for Allah.
Temporal qidam implies a beginning in time; relative qidam implies dependence on another.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم أن القدم على ثلاثة أنواع: الأول: القدم الذاتي، وهو الثابت لله تعالى وسنفسره قريباً. والثاني: القدم الزماني، وهو مستحيل على الله تعالى ويُفسر بأنه: «طول مدة وجود الشيء» فإذا قلت: عُرجُون قديم، وضلال قديم، وبناء قديم، فالمعنى الذي تدل عليه هذه العبارة أنه قد طال عليه الزمان منذ وجد ، وذلك لا ينافي أنه حادث بمعنى كون وجوده مسبوقاً بالعدم، ومن هذا قوله جل ذكره: وَالْقَمَرَ قَدَّرْنَهُ مَنَازِلَ حَتَّى عَادَ كَالْعُرْجُونِ الْقَدِيمِ ﴾ [يس: ۳۹] وقوله تباركت أسماؤه: (تَاللهِ إِنَّكَ لَفِي ضَلَلِكَ الْقَدِيمِ ﴾ [يوسف: ٩٥ ] ، والثالث: القدم الإضافي، وهو أيضا محال على الله تعالى ويفسر بأنه: «سبقُ الشيء في الوجودِ لشيء آخر» وذلك كقدَمِ الأب بالنسبة للابن. ثم إن البحث في صفة القدم يتعلق بها من جهتين إحداهما : بيان معنى القدم، والثانية: إقامة الدليل على وجوب اتصافه بالقدم. والكلام عن الجهة الأولى يستدعي أنْ نُشير لك إلى خلاف بين العلماء في صفة القدم ؛ أهي صفة نفسية كالوجود ؟ أم هي صفة سلبية كالمخالفة للحوادث؟ أم هي صفة المعاني كالعلم والقدرة ؟ فنقول : الراجح عند علماء الكلام أنَّ القدم صفةٌ سلبية ، ومعنى كونها سلبيةً أنها سلبتْ ونَفَتْ عنه ما لا يليق به سبحانه، وعلى هذا يُفسر القدم بأنه: «أن يكون وجوده تعالى غير مسبوق بعدم» أو «بكونه سبحانه لا أول لوجوده» أو «كون وجوده غير مُفتتح أي: غير مُبتدأ، فإن هذه العبارات الثلاث تؤدي معنى واحدا ، وإلى هذا جَنحَ الشارح وذهب جماعة من المتكلمين ونسبه الشيخ الملوي إلى الأشعري: إلى أن القدم صفة نفسية ، وفسَّر القدم بأنه: «الوجود المُستمر في الماضي» وهذا مذهب ضعيف واه؛ إذ لو كان القدم صفة نفسية للزم ألا تُعقَل الذَّاتُ بدونه ؛ لكنَّ الذَّات يُعقَل وجُودُها ثُمَّ يطلب البرهان على وجوب قدمها ، وإذا تُعقلت الذات موجودة في الخارج بدون احتياج في تعقلها إلى القدم لم يكن القدم صفةٌ نفسيَّةً. وأضعفُ مِن هذا المذهب قول بعضهم: إن القدم صفةٌ موجودة في الخارج تقوم بالذات كالعلم والقدرة وغيرهما من صفات المعاني، ويُنسب هذا إلى عبد الله بن سعيد بن كُلاب - بضم الكاف وتشديد اللام وآخره باء موحدة ـ ويفسر القدم على هذا المذهب بأنه: صفة قائمة بذاته تعالى
Know that qidam is of three types: First: essential qidam (al-qidam al-dhati), which is established for Allah and we will explain it soon. Second: temporal qidam (al-qidam al-zamani), which is impossible for Allah, and it is interpreted as 'the long duration of existence of a thing.' So when you say: an old palm branch, an old error, an old building, the meaning indicated by this expression is that time has extended over it since it existed, and this does not contradict it being originated in the sense that its existence is preceded by non-existence. From this is His saying: 'And the moon – We have determined for it phases until it returns like the old palm branch' and His saying: 'By Allah, indeed you were in your old error.' Third: relative qidam (al-qidam al-idafi), which is also impossible for Allah, and it is interpreted as 'the precedence of a thing in existence over another thing,' like the precedence of the father relative to the son. Then, the investigation of the attribute of qidam pertains to two aspects: one: clarifying the meaning of qidam, and the second: establishing the proof for the necessity of His being described with it. The discussion of the first aspect requires that we point out to you a disagreement among the scholars regarding the attribute of qidam: is it a self-attribute (sifa nafsiyya) like existence? Or is it a negative attribute (sifa salbiyya) like dissimilarity to originated things? Or is it an attribute of meaning (sifa ma'ani) like knowledge and power? We say: the preponderant view among the speculative theologians is that qidam is a negative attribute. The meaning of it being negative is that it negates and removes from Him what does not befit Him, Exalted is He. On this basis, qidam is interpreted as: 'that His existence, Exalted is He, is not preceded by non-existence,' or 'that He, Exalted is He, has no beginning to His existence,' or 'that His existence is not commenced, i.e., not initiated.' For these three expressions convey one meaning. And to this view inclined the commentator, and a group of theologians went, and al-Shaykh al-Malawi attributed it to al-Ash'ari: that qidam is a self-attribute, and he interpreted qidam as 'continuous existence in the past.' And this is a weak and feeble view; for if qidam were a self-attribute, then the essence would necessarily not be conceivable without it; but the essence is conceivable as existing, then a proof is sought for the necessity of its qidam. And if the essence is conceived as existing in the exterior without needing qidam in its conception, then qidam is not a self-attribute. And weaker than this view is the saying of some that qidam is an attribute existing in the exterior subsisting in the essence like knowledge and power and other attributes of meaning, and this is attributed to 'Abd Allah ibn Sa'id ibn Kullab – with a damma on the kaf, shadda on the lam, and final unified letter – and qidam on this view is interpreted as: an attribute subsisting in His essence, Exalted is He.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage defines and classifies qidam (pre-eternity). The author first distinguishes three types: essential (dhati) for God, temporal (zamani) which implies duration in time and is impossible for God, and relative (idafi) which is relative precedence also impossible for God. Then he explains the investigation of qidam has two aspects: meaning and proof. Regarding meaning, there is a disagreement among theologians: some say it is a self-attribute (nafsiyya) like existence, some say it is a negative attribute (salbiyya) like dissimilarity, and some say it is an attribute of meaning (ma'ani) like knowledge. The author states the preponderant view is that qidam is a negative attribute, and he explains the meaning: it negates that God's existence is preceded by non-existence. He then mentions that some scholars (including al-Ash'ari according to al-Malawi) consider it a self-attribute, but he refutes this: if it were a self-attribute, the essence would not be conceivable without it, yet the essence is conceivable as existing without the qidam label; thus it is not a self-attribute. Even weaker is the view of Ibn Kullab that it is an attribute of meaning subsisting in the essence.

القدم الزماني
القدم الإضافي

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Temporal qidam (long duration) is applicable to Allah.
Correction: Temporal qidam implies a beginning in time and is impossible for Allah; only essential qidam (without beginning) applies.

Checkpoint
Which types of qidam are impossible for Allah according to the passage?
A) Essential qidam only
B) Temporal and relative qidam
C) All three types
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
Qidam is of three types, but only essential qidam (without beginning) is attributed to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever think of Allah as merely 'old' or 'ancient' like a thing that has existed for a long time? How does this lesson correct that understanding and change how you relate to His eternity?
?
The lesson teaches that relative qidam, like a father before a son, is not applicable to Allah because it implies dependence. In what areas of your life have you subtly assumed Allah needs something or is limited by time? What does this call you to repent of?
?
The common misunderstanding is to confuse temporal qidam (long duration) with essential qidam (without beginning). Have you ever thought of Allah's existence as simply 'a long time' rather than 'outside of time entirely'? How does this shift your worship and reliance on Him as the Eternal One?

The Nature of Qidam: Negative, Self, or Meaning?
Dispute over the nature of qidam and defense of the negative view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three theological views on the nature of qidam and the evidence for the preponderant view that it is a negative attribute.

Core Idea
Qidam is a negative attribute, not a self-attribute or an attribute of meaning.

Having defined the types of qidam, the author now turns to a deeper question: what kind of attribute is qidam? Theologians disagreed, with three main positions. The passage presents these views and argues for the negative view, refuting the alternatives.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three views
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Look for the three views: qidam as self-attribute, negative attribute, and attribute of meaning.
The author states which view is preponderant.
2
Understand the preponderant view
The author says the preponderant view is that qidam is a negative attribute. Understand what that means: it negates that God's existence is preceded by non-existence.
The author gives three equivalent definitions.
3
Follow the refutation of the self-attribute view
The author argues that if qidam were a self-attribute, the essence would not be conceivable without it, but we can conceive of existence without qidam, so it is not a self-attribute.
This is the key argument against the view attributed to al-Ash'ari.
4
Understand the refutation of Ibn Kullab's view
The author mentions that some claim qidam is an attribute of meaning existing in the essence (like knowledge). He dismisses it as even weaker, without further argument here.

Know that qidam is of three types: First: essential qidam (al-qidam al-dhati), which is established for Allah and we will explain it soon. Second: temporal qidam (al-qidam al-zamani), which is impossible for Allah, and it is interpreted as 'the long duration of existence of a thing.' Commentary

The author first distinguishes three types: essential (dhati) for God, temporal (zamani) which implies duration in time and is impossible for God, and relative (idafi) which is relative precedence also impossible for God. Then he explains the investigation of qidam has two aspects: meaning and proof. Regarding meaning, there is a disagreement among theologians: some say it is a self-attribute (nafsiyya) like existence, some say it is a negative attribute (salbiyya) like dissimilarity, and some say it is an attribute of meaning (ma'ani) like knowledge. The author states the preponderant view is that qidam is a negative attribute, and he explains the meaning: it negates that God's existence is preceded by non-existence. He then mentions that some scholars (including al-Ash'ari according to al-Malawi) consider it a self-attribute, but he refutes this: if it were a self-attribute, the essence would not be conceivable without it, yet the essence is conceivable as existing without the qidam label; thus it is not a self-attribute. Even weaker is the view of Ibn Kullab that it is an attribute of meaning subsisting in the essence.

Key Terms
صفة نفسية
صفة سلبية
صفة المعاني
ابن كلاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Qidam is a positive attribute (self-attribute or attribute of meaning).
Correction: The author argues that qidam is a negative attribute, simply negating that God's existence is preceded by non-existence.

Checkpoint
What is the preponderant view among theologians regarding the nature of qidam according to the passage?
A) Self-attribute (nafsiyya)
B) Negative attribute (salbiyya)
C) Attribute of meaning (ma'ani)
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
The preponderant theological view is that qidam is a negative attribute, meaning God's existence is not preceded by non-existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you personally conceive of God's existence as having no beginning, or do you find yourself unconsciously imagining a starting point? How does the negative understanding of qidam force you to examine the assumptions you bring to your belief in God?
?
The author argues that qidam is not a self-attribute because the essence is conceivable without it. Does this challenge your reliance on God's eternity as a positive quality? Are you willing to trust that God's eternity is a negation of non-existence rather than a property you can fully grasp?
?
If you have ever thought that negative attributes are less significant than positive ones, how does this passage correct that? Will you now treat the negation of imperfections as a real and necessary aspect of your understanding of God?

3 min
Definition of Qidam
Sanusi defines qidam with three equivalent expressions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of qidam as the attribute of Allah having existence not preceded by non-existence, and that three expressions convey the same meaning.

Core Idea
Qidam is simple: Allah's existence has no beginning.

Sanusi opens by giving three equivalent definitions of qidam. These all express the same concept: that Allah's existence is without beginning. This foundational definition sets the stage for the theological discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of the wording. Then read the translation.
Notice that the three definitions are given in quick succession.
2
Identify the three expressions
Find each of the three phrases: 'existence not preceded by non-existence', 'no beginning', and 'existence not initiated'. Compare them.
3
Understand their equivalence
Sanusi explicitly states that these three expressions convey a single meaning. Reflect on why that is.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١ - القدم: هو أن يكون وجوده تعالى غير مسبوق بعدم. أو بكونه سبحانه لا أول لوجوده. أو كون وجوده غير مُفتتح أي: غير مُبتدأ، فإن هذه العبارات الثلاث تؤدي معنى واحدا. وإلى هذا جَنحَ الشارح وذهب جماعة من المتكلمين ونسبه الشيخ الملوي إلى الأشعري: إلى أن القدم صفة نفسية، وفسَّر القدم بأنه: «الوجود المُستمر في الماضي» وهذا مذهب ضعيف واه؛ إذ لو كان القدم صفة نفسية للزم ألا تُعقَل الذَّاتُ بدونه؛ لكنَّ الذَّات يُعقَل وجُودُها ثُمَّ يطلب البرهان على وجوب قدمها، وإذا تُعقلت الذات موجودة في الخارج بدون احتياج في تعقلها إلى القدم لم يكن القدم صفةٌ نفسيَّةً. وأضعفُ مِن هذا المذهب قول بعضهم: إن القدم صفةٌ موجودة في الخارج تقوم بالذات كالعلم والقدرة وغيرهما من صفات المعاني، ويُنسب هذا إلى عبد الله بن سعيد بن كُلاب - بضم الكاف وتشديد اللام وآخره باء موحدة ـ ويفسر القدم على هذا المذهب بأنه: صفة قائمة بذاته تعالى. والدليل على وجوب قدمه تعالى: أنه لو لم يكن قديماً لكان حادثا، إذ لا واسطة بين القدم والحدوث، ولا يجوز أن يكونَ لا قديما ولا حادثا؛ لأنَّ ذلك ارتفاع النقيضين؛ وهو مُحال كاجتماعهما، ولو كانَ حادثاً لافتقر إلى مُحدِثٍ يحدِثُه، ولو افتقر إلى مُحدث لافتقرَ مُحدِثُه إلى مُحدِثٍ؛ لأنَّ محدثه مثله، وهكذا، فإن استمر الأمر إلى ما لا نهاية لزِمَ التّسلسل، وإنْ رجع إلى الأول لزِمَ الدَّورُ، وكل منهما مُحالٌ، فما أدى إليهما ـ وهو افتقاره إلى محدث ـ محالٌ؛ فما أدى إليه - وهو كونه سبحانه مُحدثًا - مُحَالٌ، فثبتَ نَقيضُه؛ وهو كونه تعالى قديما: وهو المطلوب.
1. Al-Qidam (Preexistence): It is that His existence, may He be exalted, is not preceded by non-existence. Or that He, glory be to Him, has no beginning to His existence. Or that His existence is not initiated, i.e., not begun, for these three expressions convey a single meaning. The commentator inclined to this, and a group of theologians went along with it, and al-Shaykh al-Mallawi attributed it to al-Ash'ari: that al-qidam is an essential attribute (sifat nafsiyya). And he interpreted al-qidam as 'existence continuous in the past' – and this is a weak and flimsy doctrine. For if al-qidam were an essential attribute, then the essence would not be conceivable without it; but the essence's existence is conceivable, then proof is sought for the necessity of its preexistence. And if the essence is conceived as existent externally without needing al-qidam to conceive it, then al-qidam is not an essential attribute. Even weaker than this doctrine is the saying of some: that al-qidam is an attribute existing externally subsisting in the essence, like knowledge and power and other attributes of meanings (sifat al-ma'ani). This is attributed to 'Abdullah ibn Sa'id ibn Kullab – the letter kaf is given a damma, the lam is doubled, and the last letter is an unpointed ba' – and al-qidam is interpreted according to this doctrine as: an attribute subsisting in His essence, may He be exalted. The proof for the necessity of His preexistence, may He be exalted, is: if He were not preexistent, He would be originated, for there is no intermediate between preexistence and origination. And it is not permissible that He be neither preexistent nor originated, because that would be the negation of both contradictories, which is impossible like their conjunction. And if He were originated, He would need an originator to originate Him. And if He needed an originator, that originator would need an originator, because that originator is like Him, and so on. If the chain continues without end, infinite regress (tasalsul) would result; and if it goes back to a first, circularity (dawr) would result. Each of these is impossible. Therefore, what leads to them – which is His need for an originator – is impossible. So what leads to that – which is His being originated – is impossible. Thus its opposite is established: that He, may He be exalted, is preexistent. And that is what was sought.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of qidam (preexistence) for Allah and provides a logical proof for its necessity. The author begins by giving three equivalent definitions: that His existence is not preceded by non-existence, that He has no beginning, and that His existence is not initiated. These all mean the same thing. He then critiques two weaker interpretative positions. The first, attributed to al-Ash'ari and others, holds that qidam is an essential attribute (sifat nafsiyya), meaning the essence cannot be conceived without it. The author argues this is weak because we can conceive of the essence's existence first and then seek proof for its preexistence, which shows that qidam is not intrinsic to the essence's conception. Even weaker is the second position, attributed to Ibn Kullab, that qidam is an attribute of meaning (sifat ma'ani) subsisting externally in the essence, like knowledge and power. This is criticized as flimsy without further elaboration. The core of the passage is the proof: it proceeds by contradiction. If Allah were not preexistent, He would be originated (hadith), because there is no intermediate state between preexistence and origination (it is impossible that He be neither, as that would negate both contradictories, which is impossible). Origination implies need for an originator. That originator would in turn need an originator, leading to either an infinite regress (tasalsul) or a circularity (dawr), both impossible. Therefore the premise that He is originated is false, so the opposite – that He is preexistent – is necessarily true.

Key Terms
القدم
قديم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, how many expressions define qidam and what do they share?
A) Two expressions, same meaning
B) Three expressions, different meanings
C) Three expressions, same meaning
D) One expression only

Key Takeaway
The three definitions of qidam all point to the same truth: Allah's existence is without beginning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah has no beginning, then He alone is absolutely independent and trustworthy. Do you truly rely on Him as the Eternal One, or do you place your hope in created things that come and go? What would change this week if you lived with the certainty that Allah has always been and will always be?
?
The fact that Allah’s existence is not preceded by anything means He is the only reality that is self-sufficient. How does your awe of Allah reflect this truth? What small habit can you adopt to remind yourself daily of His eternality?
?
Sanusi repeats the same meaning three times—perhaps to emphasize that this truth must sink into the heart. Are you content with a surface intellectual acceptance of qidam, or will you work until your soul feels the weight of His eternal presence? What is one concrete step you will take today to meditate on this attribute?
