Critique of Two Interpretations of Qidam
Sanusi critiques two interpretations of qidam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi rejects the views that qidam is an essential attribute (sifat nafsiyya) or an attribute of meaning (sifat ma'ani).

Core Idea
Qidam is not an intrinsic attribute but a necessary consequence.

Sanusi presents two weaker interpretations of qidam—one from al-Ash'ari and one from Ibn Kullab—and explains why they are flawed. Understanding these mistakes clarifies the correct conception of qidam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two interpretations
Locate the two positions: (1) qidam as an essential attribute (sifat nafsiyya), (2) qidam as an attribute of meaning (sifat ma'ani).
2
Understand the first critique
Sanusi argues that if qidam were essential, the essence would be inconceivable without it, but we can conceive the essence and then prove its preexistence.
3
Understand the second critique
The second view is dismissed as even weaker, but Sanusi does not provide a detailed argument here.

Proof for Allah's Preexistence
Sanusi proves the necessity of Allah's preexistence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that Allah must be preexistent, using the categories of qidam and huduth and the impossibility of tasalsul and dawr.

Core Idea
The impossibility of infinite regress and circularity proves Allah's preexistence.

Sanusi provides a rigorous proof for Allah's preexistence by showing that the alternative—origination—leads to impossible consequences. This proof relies on the principle of non-contradiction and the impossibility of an infinite regress or circular chain of originators.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the initial dichotomy
Sanusi establishes that there is no intermediate between preexistence (qidam) and origination (huduth). So if Allah is not preexistent, He must be originated.
2
Understand the implication of origination
An originated being needs an originator (muhdith). This originator would also be originated if similar, leading to a chain.
3
Analyze the chain
The chain of originators leads to either infinite regress (tasalsul) or circularity (dawr), both deemed impossible by theologians.
4
Conclude the proof
Since both consequences are impossible, the assumption of origination is false. Therefore, Allah is preexistent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١ - القدم: هو أن يكون وجوده تعالى غير مسبوق بعدم. أو بكونه سبحانه لا أول لوجوده. أو كون وجوده غير مُفتتح أي: غير مُبتدأ، فإن هذه العبارات الثلاث تؤدي معنى واحدا. وإلى هذا جَنحَ الشارح وذهب جماعة من المتكلمين ونسبه الشيخ الملوي إلى الأشعري: إلى أن القدم صفة نفسية، وفسَّر القدم بأنه: «الوجود المُستمر في الماضي» وهذا مذهب ضعيف واه؛ إذ لو كان القدم صفة نفسية للزم ألا تُعقَل الذَّاتُ بدونه؛ لكنَّ الذَّات يُعقَل وجُودُها ثُمَّ يطلب البرهان على وجوب قدمها، وإذا تُعقلت الذات موجودة في الخارج بدون احتياج في تعقلها إلى القدم لم يكن القدم صفةٌ نفسيَّةً. وأضعفُ مِن هذا المذهب قول بعضهم: إن القدم صفةٌ موجودة في الخارج تقوم بالذات كالعلم والقدرة وغيرهما من صفات المعاني، ويُنسب هذا إلى عبد الله بن سعيد بن كُلاب - بضم الكاف وتشديد اللام وآخره باء موحدة ـ ويفسر القدم على هذا المذهب بأنه: صفة قائمة بذاته تعالى. والدليل على وجوب قدمه تعالى: أنه لو لم يكن قديماً لكان حادثا، إذ لا واسطة بين القدم والحدوث، ولا يجوز أن يكونَ لا قديما ولا حادثا؛ لأنَّ ذلك ارتفاع النقيضين؛ وهو مُحال كاجتماعهما، ولو كانَ حادثاً لافتقر إلى مُحدِثٍ يحدِثُه، ولو افتقر إلى مُحدث لافتقرَ مُحدِثُه إلى مُحدِثٍ؛ لأنَّ محدثه مثله، وهكذا، فإن استمر الأمر إلى ما لا نهاية لزِمَ التّسلسل، وإنْ رجع إلى الأول لزِمَ الدَّورُ، وكل منهما مُحالٌ، فما أدى إليهما ـ وهو افتقاره إلى محدث ـ محالٌ؛ فما أدى إليه - وهو كونه سبحانه مُحدثًا - مُحَالٌ، فثبتَ نَقيضُه؛ وهو كونه تعالى قديما: وهو المطلوب.
1. Al-Qidam (Preexistence): It is that His existence, may He be exalted, is not preceded by non-existence. Or that He, glory be to Him, has no beginning to His existence. The proof for the necessity of His preexistence, may He be exalted, is: if He were not preexistent, He would be originated, for there is no intermediate between preexistence and origination. And it is not permissible that He be neither preexistent nor originated, because that would be the negation of both contradictories, which is impossible like their conjunction. And if He were originated, He would need an originator to originate Him. And if He needed an originator, that originator would need an originator, because that originator is like Him, and so on. If the chain continues without end, infinite regress (tasalsul) would result; and if it goes back to a first, circularity (dawr) would result. Each of these is impossible. Therefore, what leads to them – which is His need for an originator – is impossible. So what leads to that – which is His being originated – is impossible. Thus its opposite is established: that He, may He be exalted, is preexistent. And that is what was sought.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of qidam (preexistence) for Allah and provides a logical proof for its necessity. The author begins by giving three equivalent definitions: that His existence is not preceded by non-existence, that He has no beginning, and that His existence is not initiated. These all mean the same thing. He then critiques two weaker interpretative positions. The first, attributed to al-Ash'ari and others, holds that qidam is an essential attribute (sifat nafsiyya), meaning the essence cannot be conceived without it. The author argues this is weak because we can conceive of the essence's existence first and then seek proof for its preexistence, which shows that qidam is not intrinsic to the essence's conception. Even weaker is the second position, attributed to Ibn Kullab, that qidam is an attribute of meaning (sifat ma'ani) subsisting externally in the essence, like knowledge and power. This is criticized as flimsy without further elaboration. The core of the passage is the proof: it proceeds by contradiction. If Allah were not preexistent, He would be originated (hadith), because there is no intermediate state between preexistence and origination (it is impossible that He be neither, as that would negate both contradictories, which is impossible). Origination implies need for an originator. That originator would in turn need an originator, leading to either an infinite regress (tasalsul) or a circularity (dawr), both impossible. Therefore the premise that He is originated is false, so the opposite – that He is preexistent – is necessarily true.

What does Sanusi argue would happen if we trace the chain of originators back indefinitely?
A) We would reach Allah

C) Nothing happens
D) The chain ends

Key Takeaway
The proof shows that origination would lead to an impossible infinite regress or circularity, so Allah must be preexistent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

The Three Opinions on Qadim and Azali
Sanusi presents three scholarly opinions on the definitions of qadim and azali and their logical relationship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three scholarly opinions on the definitions of qadim and azali and their logical relationships (generality/specificity or equality).

Core Idea
Qadim and azali are not always synonyms; their relationship depends on definition.

Before we can apply these terms to Allah, we must clarify what each term means and how they relate. The scholars have debated this, and Sanusi summarizes three distinct positions. Understanding these definitions is the key to using the terms correctly in theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the question and introduction
Start by reading the opening question that prompts the discussion. Then note that three opinions will be presented.
The question is about the difference between qadim and azali.
2
Study the first opinion
The first opinion defines qadim as an existent with no beginning, and azali as anything with no beginning (existential or not). Note the logical relationship: azali is more general.
Example: 'nothingness' (the absence of existence) is azali but not qadim.
3
Compare the second opinion
The second opinion adds the condition that qadim must also be self-subsistent (qā'im bi-nafsihi). Azali remains absolute no-beginning. The relationship is still generality/specificity.
This restricts qadim to only that which exists by itself, like Allah's Essence.
4
Examine the third opinion
The third opinion equates the two terms: both mean 'no beginning absolutely.' The relationship becomes equality.
Under this view, all attributes can be called both qadim and azali.
5
Summarize the logical relationships
Create a summary table or Venn diagram showing for each opinion whether the relationship is equality or generality/specificity.
This helps visualize the differences.

فإن قلت: فهل بين القديم والأزليّ فرقٌ؟ وإذا كان فما حد كل واحد منهما؟ فالجواب أن نقول لك: إن للعلماء في هذا الموضوع ثلاثة أقوال:
أحدها: أن القديم :هو الموجود الذي لا ابتداء لوجوده، وأما الأزلي فهو : ما لا أول له، أعمُّ أن يكون عدميًّا أو وجوديًّا، وعلى هذا تكون النسبة بين القديم والأزليّ العمومُ والخصوص المطلقُ، والأزلي أعمُّ، فكلُّ قديم أزلي وليس كلُّ أزلي قديماً.
وثاني الأقوال: أن القديم هو القائم بنفسه الذي لا أوّل لوجوده، والأزلي: الذي لا أوّل له مطلقا، سواء أكان وجوديًا أم عدميًّا وسواء أكان قائماً بنفسه أم لم يكن، وعلى هذا تكون النسبة بين القديم والأزلي العموم والخصوص المطلقُ، والأزلي أعمُّ، فكل قديم أزلي وليس كل أزلي قديماً كالأول.
والقول الثالث: أن القديم ما لا أول له مطلقا، والأزلي مثله، وعلى هذا تكون النسبة بين القديم والأزلي التّساوي فكل قديم أزلي وكل أزلي قديمٌ.
إذا علمت هذا، فاعلم أنك لو جريت على القول الأوَّل: ساغ لك أن تصف ذاته العلية وكل من صفاته الثبوتية بكل من القدم والأزلية، فتقول: الله تعالى قديم أزلي وتقول: علم الله تعالى قديم أزلي، ولا يسوغ لك أن تصف صفةً من صفاته السلبية إلّا بالأزلية فتقول: قدم الله تعالى أزلي، ولا تقول: قدم الله تعالى قديم.
ولو جريت على القول الثاني: يسوغ لك أن تصف ذاته تعالى بكلِّ مِن القدم والأزليَّة، فتقول: الله تعالى قديم أزلي، ولا يسوغ لك أن تصف صفةً من صفاته سبحانه بالقدم، وتصفها بالأزليَّة، فتقول : علم الله أزلي، ولا تقول: علم الله تعالى قديم.
وإذا جريت على القول الثالث: ساغ لك أن تصف ذاته سبحانه بالقدم والأزلية، وساغ لك أيضا أن تصف كل صفة من صفاته بكل من القدم والأزلية، فتقول: الله تعالى قديم أزلي، وقدم الله تعالى قديم أزلي، وعلم الله تعالى قديم أزلي، فاعرف هذا فإنه مما يحتاج إليه.
If you say: Is there a difference between al-qadim (the preexistent) and al-azali (the eternal)? And if so, what is the definition of each? The answer is to say to you: The scholars have three opinions on this subject:
One of them: that al-qadim is the existent that has no beginning to its existence, while al-azali is that which has no beginning, whether it be non-existential or existential. According to this, the relationship between al-qadim and al-azali is absolute generality and specificity; al-azali is more general, so every qadim is azali, but not every azali is qadim.
The second opinion: that al-qadim is the self-subsistent (qā'im bi-nafsihi) that has no beginning to its existence, while al-azali is that which has no beginning absolutely, whether existential or non-existential, and whether self-subsistent or not. According to this, the relationship is also absolute generality and specificity, al-azali being more general, so every qadim is azali, but not every azali is qadim, like the first.
The third opinion: that al-qadim is that which has no beginning absolutely, and al-azali is like it. According to this, the relationship between them is equality, so every qadim is azali and every azali is qadim.
Now that you know this, know that if you follow the first opinion, it is permissible for you to describe the Lofty Essence and each of His positive attributes (sifāt thubūtiyya) with both preexistence and eternity, so you say: Allah is qadim and azali, and you say: Allah's knowledge is qadim and azali. But it is not permissible for you to describe any of His negative attributes (sifāt salbiyya) except with eternity, so you say: Allah's preexistence is azali, and you do not say: Allah's preexistence is qadim.
If you follow the second opinion, it is permissible for you to describe His Essence, may He be exalted, with both preexistence and eternity, so you say: Allah is qadim and azali. But it is not permissible for you to describe any of His attributes, glory be to Him, with preexistence; rather you describe them with eternity, so you say: Allah's knowledge is azali, and you do not say: Allah's knowledge is qadim.
If you follow the third opinion, it is permissible for you to describe His Essence, glory be to Him, with preexistence and eternity, and it is also permissible for you to describe every attribute of His attributes with both preexistence and eternity, so you say: Allah is qadim azali, and Allah's preexistence is qadim azali, and Allah's knowledge is qadim azali. Know this, for it is something that is needed.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is an expository answer to a question about the difference between the terms qadim and azali. The author presents three scholarly opinions on their definitions and the logical relationship between them, then applies each opinion to determine what may be described by each term in reference to Allah and His attributes.

The first opinion defines qadim as an existent with no beginning to its existence, while azali is anything with no beginning, whether existential or non-existential. Thus azali is more general: every qadim is azali, but not every azali is qadim. According to this opinion, positive attributes (like knowledge) can be called both qadim and azali, but negative attributes (like qidam itself, which is a relational concept) can only be called azali, not qadim, because they are not existent in the same sense.

The second opinion adds that qadim is also self-subsistent (qā'im bi-nafsihi), whereas azali is simply without beginning irrespective of subsistence. Again azali is more general. Under this opinion, only the Divine Essence can be called qadim; attributes like knowledge can only be called azali, because they are not self-subsistent.

The third opinion equates the two terms: both mean 'without beginning absolutely,' so the relationship is equality, and both the Essence and all attributes can be described by both terms.

The passage ends with a strong admonition: 'Know this, for it is something that is needed.'

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many people assume qadim and azali are exact synonyms and can always be used interchangeably.
Correction: The first two opinions show that azali is broader in scope. For example, non-existence is azali but not qadim. Only the third opinion equates them.

Checkpoint
According to the first opinion, which of the following is true?
A) Every azali is qadim.
B) Every qadim is azali.
C) Qadim and azali are equal.
D) The relationship is like water and ice.

Key Takeaway
The terms qadim and azali have different definitions according to different opinions, affecting their logical relationship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The scholars differed on whether qadim and azali are synonymous. How does the precision of these terms affect the way you think about Allah's eternity? Does your mind settle on a vague 'forever' or a sharp 'no beginning at all'? Commit to using precise language when describing Allah's attributes, even in your private thoughts.
?
If non-existence can be described as azali but not qadim (according to the first two opinions), what does that imply about the absolute priority of Allah? When you consider that everything other than Allah is either originated or even non-existent in the past, does that humble your heart? Choose one area of your life where you act as if something else is 'eternal'—like a career or a relationship—and ask Allah to replace that attachment with true devotion to Him.
?
The second opinion adds the condition of self-subsistence (qā'im bi-nafsihi) for something to be called qadim. In what ways do you depend on others for your existence and identity? How can you cultivate a reliance only on Allah? Identify one habit today that reflects dependence on a created being, and replace it with an act of tawakkul.

Applying Qadim and Azali to Allah's Attributes
Sanusi explains how each opinion on qadim and azali affects the permissibility of describing Allah's Essence and attributes as qadim or azali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how each of the three opinions on qadim and azali affects what can be ascribed to Allah's Essence and His attributes (positive vs negative).

Core Idea
Which divine attributes can be called qadim depends on whether they are self-subsistent and positive.

The definitions have immediate consequences: what may we say about Allah? Sanusi applies each opinion to the Divine Essence, positive attributes (like knowledge), and negative attributes (like preexistence). Understanding these applications is crucial for accurate theological formulations.

Guided Path
1
Read the application for the first opinion
Under the first opinion, you may call Allah's Essence and positive attributes both qadim and azali, but negative attributes (like qidam) only azali.
Negative attributes are not 'existents' in the same way, so they cannot be qadim.
2
Study the second opinion
Under the second opinion, only Allah's Essence can be called qadim. Attributes, even positive ones, cannot be called qadim because they are not self-subsistent. They can only be called azali.
This is stricter: attributes are considered not self-subsistent.
3
Examine the third opinion
Under the third opinion, both the Essence and all attributes can be called both qadim and azali without restriction.
This is the broadest application.
4
Compare the three opinions
Create a table with rows: Essence, positive attributes, negative attributes. Columns: first opinion, second opinion, third opinion. Fill in whether each can be called qadim, azali, or both.
This will highlight the differences.
5
Memorize the author's warning
The author ends with 'Know this, for it is something that is needed.' This emphasizes the practical importance of these distinctions in theological discourse.
It is a call to carefully apply the correct terminology.

If you say: Is there a difference between al-qadim (the preexistent) and al-azali (the eternal)? And if so, what is the definition of each? The answer is to say to you: The scholars have three opinions on this subject:
One of them: that al-qadim is the existent that has no beginning to its existence, while al-azali is that which has no beginning, whether it be non-existential or existential. The third opinion: that al-qadim is that which has no beginning absolutely, and al-azali is like it. According to this, the relationship between them is equality, so every qadim is azali and every azali is qadim.

This passage is an expository answer to a question about the difference between the terms qadim and azali. The author presents three scholarly opinions on their definitions and the logical relationship between them, then applies each opinion to determine what may be described by each term in reference to Allah and His attributes.

Permissibility of Using 'Qadim' for Allah
Sanusi frames a question about the permissibility of uttering 'qadim' as a name for Allah, presenting two opposing views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two scholarly positions on whether it is permissible to explicitly call Allah 'al-qadim' and the principle of tawqifiyya that underlies the cautious view.

Core Idea
Whether a divine attribute is proven does not automatically permit using its derived name; names require scriptural authorization.

Sanusi presents a classic theological question: can we say 'Allah is qadim' directly, given that the attribute of preexistence is established by reason and revelation? One view permits it via derivation; the other restricts it due to the principle that divine names are tawqifiyya, requiring explicit revelation. This lesson examines both positions and their foundations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the question. Notice that the passage presents two opposing views without reaching a conclusion.
The passage is incomplete; it cuts off at the page break.
2
Identify the two positions
The first view argues that since the meaning of qidam is proven, one may derive and use the name. The second view cautions against using 'qadim' directly because names must be based on revelation.
The second view recommends descriptive phrases instead.
3
Reflect on the tawqifiyya principle
Consider why some scholars insist that divine names require scriptural authorization, and how this affects theological language.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت: هل يجوز أن يُتلفظ بلفظ القديم في حقه فيقال: «الله قديم» بناء على أن معنى القدم ثابت له سبحانه عقلا ونقلا، ومن ثبت له شيءٌ صح أن يُشتقَ له منه اسم، أو أنه ينبغي ألا يتلفظ بذلك، وإنما يكتفى بأن يُقال: يجب له القدم، أو يجب له عدم الأولية، أو يجب له عدم افتتاح الوجود، ونحو ذلك مما قام دليل العقل والنقل عليه، بناءً على أنَّ أسماء توقيفية، أي : يتوقف جواز إطلاق كلّ واحد منها على نص من الشارع، فما ورد عن الشَّارع إطلاقه عليه جاز لنا أن نطلقه عليه ، وما لم يرد عن الشارع إطلاقه عليه =
If you say: Is it permissible to utter the term 'al-qadim' concerning Him, saying 'Allah is qadim', on the basis that the meaning of preexistence (qidam) is established for Him, glory be to Him, by reason and revelation, and whoever has something established for him, it is valid to derive a name for him from it? Or should one not utter that, but rather suffice with saying: 'Preexistence is necessary for Him' or 'Non-originality is necessary for Him' or 'Non-initiation of existence is necessary for Him,' and the like, of what the evidence of reason and revelation has established, on the basis that names are tawqifiyya (dependent on divine authorization), i.e., the permissibility of applying each one depends on a text from the Lawgiver; so whatever the Lawgiver has authorized applying to Him, we may apply to Him, and whatever the Lawgiver has not authorized applying to Him =
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a question (su'āl) about the permissibility of actively using the name 'al-qadim' for Allah. The question presents two opposing positions. The first position argues that since the meaning of qidam (preexistence) is rationally and scripturally proven for Allah, we may derive from that meaning a name and say 'Allah is qadim.' This is based on the principle that if an attribute is proven, one can coin a name from it. The second position warns against explicitly uttering 'qadim' and instead recommends using descriptive phrases like 'preexistence is necessary for Him' or 'non-originality is necessary for Him.' This caution stems from the doctrine that the divine names are tawqifiyya, meaning they require explicit scriptural authorization. Since 'al-qadim' as a name is not directly attested in revelation, some scholars hesitate to apply it as a name, even though the meaning is affirmed. The passage cuts off at the point of explaining the ruling according to the second view, but the question sets up the issue clearly.

Key Terms
قديم
أسماء توقيفية
اشتقاق
الشارع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If an attribute is proven, its derived name is automatically permitted.
Correction: The tawqifiyya principle can restrict naming to explicitly revealed names, so even if the attribute is proven, the derived name may not be permitted without scriptural authorization.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of disagreement in this passage regarding the term 'qadim'?
A) Whether Allah is actually preexistent.
B) Whether the meaning of qidam is known by reason or revelation.
C) Whether it is permissible to utter 'qadim' as a name for Allah or only to describe Him with phrases.
D) Whether 'qadim' and 'azali' are synonymous.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of applying a name to Allah depends not only on the attribute being true but also on whether the name itself has been authorized by revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you call upon Allah using a name not explicitly in the Qur'an or Sunnah, does it ever trouble your conscience that you might be overstepping the bounds of reverence? How would you investigate whether a name is authorized?
?
The passage shows that even a true attribute does not automatically give you license to name. Is there a name for Allah that you use casually without having verified its scriptural basis? Will you pause today to check?
?
If you were to defend the use of 'al-Qadim' for Allah in a discussion, could you honestly say you have weighed the tawqifiyyah principle? Would you rather rely on reason alone or submit to revelation's limits?

First Opinion: Describing Essence and Positive Attributes
Application of the first opinion to divine essence and attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the permissible descriptions of Allah's essence and attributes under the first opinion regarding qidam and azaliyya.

Core Idea
Under the first opinion, only essence and positive attributes can be called qadīm.

This lesson applies the first opinion to the language of divine descriptions. According to this view, qidam is an attribute that subsists only in the essence itself, not in other attributes. Therefore, it affects which terms we can use for essence, positive attributes, and negative attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the first opinion
Carefully read the Arabic and its translation for the first opinion, noting the rules for essence, positive attributes, and negative attributes.
2
Identify the allowed statements
List the statements permitted and prohibited under this opinion. Notice the distinction between positive and negative attributes.
Negative attributes like qidam itself can only be called azalī, not qadīm.
3
Reflect on the rationale
Consider why the first opinion makes this distinction. It is based on the nature of qidam as an essential attribute of the essence itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا علمت هذا ، فاعلم أنك لو جريت على القول الأوَّل: ساغ لك أن تصف ذاته العلية وكل من صفاته الثبوتية بكل من القدم والأزلية، فتقول: الله تعالى قديم أزلي وتقول: علم الله تعالى قديم أزلي، ولا يسوغ لك أن تصف صفةً من صفاته السلبية إلّا بالأزلية فتقول: قدم الله تعالى أزلي، ولا تقول : قدم الله تعالى قديم. ولو جريت على القول الثاني: يسوغ لك أن تصف ذاته تعالى بكلِّ مِن القدم والأزليَّة ، فتقول: الله تعالى قديم أزلي، ولا يسوغ لك أن تصف صفةً من صفاته سبحانه بالقدم، وتصفها بالأزليَّة ، فتقول : علم الله أزلي، ولا تقول: علم الله تعالى قديم . وإذا جريت على القول الثالث: ساغ لك أن تصف ذاته سبحانه بالقدم والأزلية، وساغ لك أيضا أن تصف كل صفة من صفاته بكل من القدم والأزلية ، فتقول: الله تعالى قديم أزلي، وقدم الله تعالى قديم أزلي، وعلم الله تعالى قديم أزلي، فاعرف هذا فإنه مما يحتاج إليه.
If you know this, then know that if you follow the first opinion: it is permissible for you to describe His sublime essence and each of His positive attributes with both qidam and azaliyya, so you say: 'Allah Most High is qadīm azalī', and you say: 'Allah's knowledge is qadīm azalī'. But it is not permissible for you to describe any of His negative attributes except with azaliyya, so you say: 'Allah's qidam is azalī', and you do not say: 'Allah's qidam is qadīm'. And if you follow the second opinion: it is permissible for you to describe His essence Most High with both qidam and azaliyya, so you say: 'Allah Most High is qadīm azalī', but it is not permissible for you to describe any of His attributes, glory be to Him, with qidam; rather you describe them with azaliyya, so you say: 'Allah's knowledge is azalī', and you do not say: 'Allah's knowledge is qadīm'. And if you follow the third opinion: it is permissible for you to describe His essence glory be to Him with qidam and azaliyya, and it is also permissible for you to describe every attribute of His with both qidam and azaliyya, so you say: 'Allah Most High is qadīm azalī', and 'Allah's qidam is qadīm azalī', and 'Allah's knowledge is qadīm azalī'. So know this, for it is something needed.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage applies the three preceding opinions to the practical theological issue of how to describe God's essence and attributes. The author explains the permissible formulations under each opinion. Under the first opinion, only God's essence and positive attributes (ṣifāt thubūtiyya) can be called both qadīm and azalī; negative attributes (ṣifāt salbiyya) such as qidam itself (the attribute of being eternal) can only be described as azalī, not qadīm. Under the second opinion, even positive attributes cannot be called qadīm because they are not self-subsistent; they are only azalī. Under the third opinion, both essence and all attributes can be described with both terms. The author concludes by emphasizing the practical importance of these distinctions.

صفات ثبوتية
صفات سلبية
قدم
أزلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That negative attributes like qidam can be called qadīm.
Correction: Under the first opinion, negative attributes are not self-subsistent and therefore cannot be described as qadīm; they are only azalī.

Checkpoint

B) 'Allah's knowledge is qadīm azalī'
C) 'Allah's qidam is qadīm'
D) 'Allah's power is azalī'

Key Takeaway
Under the first opinion, only Allah's essence and positive attributes are described as qadīm; negative attributes are only azalī.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The lesson teaches that even Allah's attributes like knowledge are eternal. Does the fact that Allah's knowledge is without beginning give you comfort or fear? How should it affect the way you live right now?
?

Second Opinion: Attributes Cannot Be Called Qadīm
Application of the second opinion to divine essence and attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the permissible descriptions under the second opinion, which restricts calling attributes qadīm.

Core Idea
Under the second opinion, only the essence can be called qadīm; attributes are only azalī.

The second opinion holds that qidam is a mode of existence that applies directly only to the essence. Attributes, being dependent on the essence, cannot be described as qadīm in themselves. This lesson applies that view to the permissible forms of description.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the second opinion
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the rule that only the essence can be qadīm, and attributes can only be azalī.
2
Contrast with the first opinion
Compare the second opinion to the first. Notice that the second opinion is more restrictive: even positive attributes cannot be called qadīm.
3
Practice the formulations
Write statements for essence and for attributes under this opinion, ensuring you do not call any attribute qadīm.

Third Opinion: Full Permissibility for Essence and All Attributes
Application of the third opinion: full permissibility for all divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that under the third opinion, both the essence and all attributes can be described as qadīm azalī.

Core Idea
Under the third opinion, every divine attribute can be called qadīm azalī like the essence.

The third opinion takes a unifying view: qidam and azaliyya are coextensive and apply to all that is attributable to Allah, whether essence or attribute. This lesson shows the practical outcome of this opinion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the third opinion
Read the Arabic and translation, noting that there is no restriction: essence and all attributes can be described with both terms.
2
Compare with the first two opinions
Notice how this opinion is the most permissive, allowing every attribute to be called qadīm azalī.
3
Memorize the conclusion
The author emphasizes to 'know this, for it is something needed.' Understand the practical importance of these distinctions.

Definition of Qidam as a Negative Attribute
Definition of qidam as a negative attribute and clarification on the scope of its particulars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what qidam means as a negative attribute and why its particulars are not limited to five.

Core Idea
Qidam negates what is unbefitting: its particulars are countless, not just five.

Sanusi defines qidam as a negative attribute — the negation of anything unbefitting to Allah. He clarifies that the particulars of such attributes are not limited, although five are famously enumerated as foundational. This lesson unpacks that definition and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
First, carefully read the Arabic text and its literal English translation. Pay attention to the terms used.
Notice the phrase "ليست جزئياته حصرة" which means "its particulars are not limited".
2
Identify the definition of qidam
Find the definition: qidam is every attribute whose meaning is the negation of something unbefitting to God.
This defines qidam as a negative attribute (sifah salbiyyah).
3
Understand the concept of a negative attribute
A negative attribute affirms absence, not presence. Here, it negates non-existence prior to existence.
4
Grasp the point about particulars not being limited
The author states that the particulars (individual instances) of this attribute are not limited to a specific number.
This is the correct view, contrary to some who might think only five exist.
5
Note the reason for enumerating five and why qidam is first
Some scholars enumerated five key negative attributes because they are important "mothers." Qidam is given precedence because later attributes depend on it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أ - القدم هي: كل صفة مدلولها عدمُ أمر لا يليق به سبحانه. وليست جزئياته حصرةً على الصَّحيح (۱) ، وعدَّ منها خمسة تبعا لبعضهم؛ لأنَّها من مُهمات أُمَّهاتها ، وقدَّم منها القِدَم لابتناء ما بعده عليه(٢).
A - al-qidam: it is every attribute whose meaning is the negation of something unbefitting to Him, glory be to Him. And its particulars are not limited according to the correct view, and five were enumerated following some of them because they are among the important mothers of them, and among them qidam was given precedence because what comes after it is built upon it.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage defines qidam (eternity) as a negative attribute (ṣifa salbiyya): it is the negation of anything unbefitting God, specifically the negation of non-existence prior to existence. The author notes that the particulars of this negative attribute are not limited; in the correct view, there is no finite list. However, some scholars have enumerated five key negative attributes, including qidam, because they are the most fundamental 'mothers' (ummahāt) of the category. Qidam is given precedence because other negative attributes (like baqā' or mukhālafah) depend on it. The passage sets the stage for a more detailed discussion of the five negative attributes.

Key Terms
القدم
صفة سلبية
جزئيات
عدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The five negative attributes (qidam, baqa, etc.) are the only ones that exist.
Correction: The author explicitly says 'its particulars are not limited' — the five are just prominent examples, not an exhaustive list.

Checkpoint
According to the correct view, are the particulars of negative attributes limited?
A) Yes, exactly five.
B) Yes, but only the important ones.
C) No, they are not limited.
D) No, but only if they are not from the mothers.

Key Takeaway
Qidam is a negative attribute meaning the negation of any unworthiness; its scope is not confined to five items.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly negate every unworthy thought or image of God from your heart, or do you sometimes limit His perfection without realizing it? What specific unbefitting assumption about God will you actively reject today?
?
The lesson says qidam's particulars are not limited—there is no end to the ways God is free from imperfection. How does this truth confront your tendency to confine God to your own understanding? What will you do this week to expand your awe of His absolute perfection?
?
If qidam (eternity without beginning) is the foundation for all other divine attributes, how does the reality of a God unbound by time challenge your daily trust in His promises? What is one situation where you have acted as if God's timelessness does not apply, and how will you repent from that today?

Negative Attributes and Their Unbounded Particulars
Definition of qidam and the ruling on its particulars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of negative attributes (specifically qidam) and the correct view that their particulars are not limited to a fixed enumeration.

Core Idea
Negative attributes negate the unbefitting, and their particulars are unbounded.

Sanusi begins by defining one of the most fundamental negative attributes: qidam (past eternity). He explains that its meaning is the negation of anything unbefitting to Allah. He then addresses a dispute: are the particulars of such attributes limited or not? The correct view, he states, is that they are not limited, though some scholars count five key ones.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of negative attributes
Read the first sentence: 'al-qidam is every attribute whose meaning is the negation of something unbefitting to Allah.' This establishes the core concept.
Negative attributes are about what Allah is not.
2
Grasp the dispute about enumeration
Notice the phrase 'its particulars are not limited according to the correct view'. Then he mentions that he counted five following some scholars. Understand that this is a pedagogical choice, not a doctrinal limit.
3
Appreciate the arrangement of attributes
He says he presented qidam first because later attributes are built upon it. Realize that qidam is foundational among negative attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القدم هي: كل صفة مدلولها عدمُ أمر لا يليق به سبحانه. وليست جزئياته حصرةً على الصحيح، وعدَّ منها خمسة تبعا لبعضهم؛ لأنَّها من مُهمات أُمَّهاتها، وقدَّم منها القِدَم لابتناء ما بعده عليه، يعني وواجب له تعالى لا يجوز لنا أن نطلقه عليه، ولو كان معناه صحيحا. والجواب عن هذا أن نقول لك: من الناس من نقل إطلاق الشارع لفظ القديم عليه تعالى، وعلى هذا يكون إطلاقه سائغاً حتى عند من ذهب إلى أن أسماءه توقيفيَّةٌ، ومن الناس من لم يطلع على ما ورد عن الشارع فتردَّد في جواز إطلاق هذا الاسم عليه، وليس التّردُّد خاصا يبيح إطلاقه، بلفظ القديم، بل هو جارٍ في كل اسم يقتضي مدحاً خالصاً، ولا يوهم نقصاً ولم يكن قد ورد عن الشارع نصّ إطلاقه على الله سبحانه، فإن أوهم الاسم نقصاً أو لم يكن مدحاً خالصاً فالإجماع منعقد على عدم جواز إطلاقه عليه، وإن ورد عن الشارع نص يبيح فالإجماع منعقد على إباحة إطلاقه، فاعرف هذا.
Al-Qidam (past eternity) is: every attribute whose meaning is the negation of a thing unbefitting to Him, Exalted. And its particulars are not limited according to the correct view, and he counted five following some scholars, because they are among the important mothers of them, and he presented al-qidam due to what follows it being built upon it. Meaning, it is obligatory for Him, Exalted, [but] it is not permissible for us to apply it to Him, even if its meaning is correct. And the answer to this is that we say to you: Among people are those who transmitted the Lawgiver's usage of the word 'al-Qadim' for Him, Exalted, and on this its usage is permissible even according to those who hold that His names are tawqifiyya (restricted to revelation). And among people are those who did not come across what came from the Lawgiver, so they hesitated about the permissibility of applying this name to Him. And hesitation is not specific to the word 'al-Qadim', but rather it applies to every name that implies pure praise, does not imply deficiency, and for which no text from the Lawgiver has come permitting its application to Allah, Exalted. For if the name implies deficiency or is not pure praise, then the consensus is established on its impermissibility. And if a text from the Lawgiver permits it, then the consensus is established on its permissibility. Know this.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage defines the negative attributes (al-sifat al-salbiyya) and addresses a dispute about their enumeration. The author begins by defining 'al-qidam' as a type of negative attribute: it is every attribute whose meaning is the negation of something unbefitting to Allah. He then states that according to the correct view, the particulars of these negative attributes are not limited to a fixed number, though some scholars have enumerated five core ones. He then moves to a related issue: although the meaning of 'qadim' is correct (denoting eternal existence), some object that we cannot call Allah by this name unless it is revealed. The response distinguishes two positions: those who know that the Lawgiver used the term 'Qadim' for Allah may use it, even among those who hold that Allah's names are tawqifiyya (restricted to revelation). Those who have no such knowledge should hesitate, but this hesitation is not limited to 'Qadim'—it applies to any name that is pure praise, does not imply deficiency, and has no explicit revelatory permission. If a name implies deficiency or is not pure praise, consensus forbids it; if revelation permits it, consensus permits it.

Key Terms
قدم
صفات سلبية
جزئيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the negative attributes are limited to exactly five.
Correction: The text clearly states that the correct view is that they are not limited. The five mentioned are just a selection.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct view regarding the particulars of negative attributes?
A) They are limited to five.
B) They are not limited.
C) They are limited to those mentioned in revelation.
D) They are limited to qidam only.

Key Takeaway
Negative attributes negate what is unbefitting to Allah, and their particulars are not restricted to a fixed number.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you picture Allah in your mind, do you unconsciously limit His perfection to just a few negations (like 'He is not born') while ignoring countless other unworthy thoughts you might harbor? What specific negation will you consciously affirm today to purify your understanding?
?
The lesson says qidam is foundational—without it, other attributes collapse. Is your conviction of Allah's eternal existence truly the bedrock of your worship, or have you built your faith on something less certain? What would change if you let this truth govern your daily actions?
?
If the particulars of negative attributes are unbounded, that means there is an infinite number of ways you could think unworthily of Allah—and you likely do without realizing it. Will you commit to examining your heart daily to uproot any subtle notion that diminishes His majesty? What is one such notion you currently hold?

Applying the Name 'Qadim' to Allah and the Principle of Tawqif
Answering the objection to using 'Qadim' as a divine name

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate about calling Allah 'Qadim' and the broader rule for using names that are not explicitly revealed.

Core Idea
Calling Allah by a name requires either revelatory permission or absence of deficiency and pure praise.

After defining qidam, Sanusi addresses an important issue: though the meaning of 'Qadim' is correct, can we actually use it as a name for Allah? Some object that we cannot, since it is not explicitly revealed. Sanusi answers by explaining that if there is a report of the Lawgiver using it, it is allowed; if not, one should hesitate, but this hesitation applies to any name that is pure praise and not implying deficiency. He outlines the consensus on such matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the part: 'it is not permissible for us to apply it to Him, even if its meaning is correct.' Understand the objection: some say we cannot use 'Qadim' because it is not a revealed name.
This objection comes from the principle of tawqifiyya.
2
Understand the two categories of people
The response divides people into two groups: those who know the Lawgiver used it (and thus may use it) and those who haven't seen evidence (and thus hesitate). Note that hesitation is not unique to 'Qadim' but applies to any name that is pure praise and without deficiency.
3
Learn the general rule for divine names
The passage concludes that any name implying deficiency or not being pure praise is forbidden by consensus; any name with revelatory permission is allowed. This is a key principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القدم هي: كل صفة مدلولها عدمُ أمر لا يليق به سبحانه. وليست جزئياته حصرةً على الصحيح، وعدَّ منها خمسة تبعا لبعضهم؛ لأنَّها من مُهمات أُمَّهاتها، وقدَّم منها القِدَم لابتناء ما بعده عليه، يعني وواجب له تعالى لا يجوز لنا أن نطلقه عليه، ولو كان معناه صحيحا. والجواب عن هذا أن نقول لك: من الناس من نقل إطلاق الشارع لفظ القديم عليه تعالى، وعلى هذا يكون إطلاقه سائغاً حتى عند من ذهب إلى أن أسماءه توقيفيَّةٌ، ومن الناس من لم يطلع على ما ورد عن الشارع فتردَّد في جواز إطلاق هذا الاسم عليه، وليس التّردُّد خاصا يبيح إطلاقه، بلفظ القديم، بل هو جارٍ في كل اسم يقتضي مدحاً خالصاً، ولا يوهم نقصاً ولم يكن قد ورد عن الشارع نصّ إطلاقه على الله سبحانه، فإن أوهم الاسم نقصاً أو لم يكن مدحاً خالصاً فالإجماع منعقد على عدم جواز إطلاقه عليه، وإن ورد عن الشارع نص يبيح فالإجماع منعقد على إباحة إطلاقه، فاعرف هذا.
Al-Qidam (past eternity) is: every attribute whose meaning is the negation of a thing unbefitting to Him, Exalted. Meaning, it is obligatory for Him, Exalted, [but] it is not permissible for us to apply it to Him, even if its meaning is correct. And the answer to this is that we say to you: Among people are those who transmitted the Lawgiver's usage of the word 'al-Qadim' for Him, Exalted, and on this its usage is permissible even according to those who hold that His names are tawqifiyya (restricted to revelation). And among people are those who did not come across what came from the Lawgiver, so they hesitated about the permissibility of applying this name to Him. And hesitation is not specific to the word 'al-Qadim', but rather it applies to every name that implies pure praise, does not imply deficiency, and for which no text from the Lawgiver has come permitting its application to Allah, Exalted. For if the name implies deficiency or is not pure praise, then the consensus is established on its impermissibility. And if a text from the Lawgiver permits it, then the consensus is established on its permissibility. Know this.

Al-Baqa': The Everlastingness of Allah
Defines baqa' as impossibility of ceasing to exist and rejects temporal continuity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that al-baqa' is a negative attribute meaning the impossibility of non-existence for Allah, and why interpreting it as temporal continuation is incorrect.

Core Idea
Allah's everlastingness is not temporal duration but the impossibility of ceasing to exist.

This lesson examines the second negative attribute: al-baqa' (everlastingness). The author, Sanusi, defines it precisely to prevent a common misunderstanding that would imply time applies to Allah. Understanding this sets the foundation for affirming Allah's transcendence beyond temporal categories.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the definition
The passage defines baqa' as 'the impossibility of non-existence attaching to His existence'. See how this links to qidam (pre-eternity).
3
Understand the rejection of temporal continuity
The phrase 'it is not mixed with non-existence' guards against interpreting baqa' as temporal extension. Ask why time cannot apply to Allah.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كذا أي كوجوب الوجود والقدم له تعالى بقاء وهو الصفة الثانية من الصفات السلبية، ومعناه: امتناع لحوق العدم لوجوده؛ لأنَّ ما ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه. ووصف البقاء بقوله: لا يشاب أي لا يخالط بالعدم ولا يلحقه ليحترز به عن البقاء بمعنى مقارنة استمرار الوجود زمانين فصاعدا، لاستحالته عليه تعالى بهذا المعنى؛ لامتناع دخول الزمان في وجوده تعالى وسائر صفاته.
Likewise, i.e., like the necessity of existence and al-qidam, for Him, Exalted, is al-baqa' (everlastingness), and it is the second attribute of the negative attributes. Its meaning is: the impossibility of non-existence attaching to His existence; because that whose qidam is established, its non-existence is impossible. He described al-baqa' by His saying: 'it is not mixed' i.e., it is not mixed with non-existence nor does it attach to it, to guard against al-baqa' in the sense of the co-occurrence of the continuance of existence for two times or more, because this meaning is impossible for Him, Exalted, due to the impossibility of time entering into His existence, Exalted, and all His attributes.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage defines al-baqa' (everlastingness) as the second negative attribute for Allah. Its meaning is the impossibility of non-existence ever attaching to His existence; anything whose past eternity (qidam) is established cannot cease to exist. The author then clarifies the correct understanding by quoting the phrase 'it is not mixed with non-existence', which guards against a mistaken interpretation of baqa' as the mere continuation of existence over two or more temporal periods. Such temporal continuity is impossible for Allah because time itself does not apply to His existence or attributes. Thus baqa' is a negative attribute, denying the possibility of annihilation, not affirming temporal extension.

Key Terms
بقاء
صفات سلبية
عدم
زمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Baqa' means Allah's existence continues through time.
Correction: Baqa' is the impossibility of non-existence, not temporal extension, because time does not apply to Allah.

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator reject interpreting baqa' as 'continuance of existence over two times or more'?
A) Because Allah is not subject to time.
B) Because Allah's existence is limited.
C) Because baqa' only applies to created beings.
D) Because the Qur'an does not mention it.

Key Takeaway
Al-baqa' is a negative attribute: Allah cannot cease to exist, and His everlastingness has no relation to time.

Definition of al-Baqa' as a Negative Attribute
Sanusi defines al-Baqa' as a negative attribute and clarifies its meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fundamental definition of al-Baqa' as the second negative attribute of Allah, meaning the impossibility of non-existence attaching to His existence.

Core Idea
Al-Baqa' is not about time but about impossibility of non-existence.

Sanusi begins his discussion of al-Baqa' by placing it among the negative attributes and giving its precise meaning. He immediately clarifies that 'remaining' for Allah does not involve time, because time itself is a created entity. This lesson establishes the core definition that the rest of the discussion builds upon.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the phrase 'impossibility of non-existence attaching to His existence' and how it connects to eternity (qidam).
The definition is concise but packed with meaning.
2
Understand the poem's phrase
The author explains the poem's phrase 'la yushabu bil-'adam' (it is not mixed with non-existence) as a guard against the temporal sense of perpetuity.
3
Reflect on the time issue
Ask yourself: why does the author immediately exclude time from the definition? How does that relate to Allah's transcendence?
This is a key point for later lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من [٢ - البقاء] (كَذَا ) أي : كوجُوبِ الوجُودِ والقِدَم له تعالى (بَقَاءُ) وهو الصفة الثانية الصَّفات السلبية، ومعناه: امتناع لحوق العدم لوجوده ؛ لأنَّ ما ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه. ووصَفَ البقاء بقوله: (لَا يُشَابُ) أي: لا يُخَالط (بِالْعَدَم) ولا يَلْحَقه ؛ ليحتَرِزَ به عن البقاء بمعنى مقارنة استمرار الوجود زمانين فصاعدا، لاستحالته عليه تعالى بهذا المعنى ؛ لامتناع دخول الزمان في وجوده تعالى وسائر صفاته. وقد جرى بين العلماء خلاف في معنى البقاء كالخلاف الجاري بينهم في معنى القدم، وهذا الخلاف مبني على خلاف آخر حاصله: هل البقاء صفة سلبية أم هو صفة نفسية كالوجود ؟ أم هو صفة من صفات المعاني ؟ فمن العلماء من زعم أن البقاء صفة نفسية كالوجود وفسره بأنه: «الوجود المستمر فيما لا يزال» ، أي : في المستقبل إلى غير نهاية، وممن ذهب إلى هذا القاضي أبوبكر، وإمام الحرمين، والرازي، ومعتزلة البصرة. ومنهم من زعم أنه صفة من صفات المعاني، كالعلم، والقدرة، وفسره: «بأنه صفة قائمة بالذات الأقدس، لها وجود زائد على وجود الذات»، وممن ذهب إلى هذا الشيخ أبو الحسن، ومعتزلة بغداد، وهذان الرأيان ضعيفان، والراجح أن البقاء : صفة سلبية، وأن معناه : نفي العدم اللاحق بعد الوجود أو الثبوت» وإن شئت قلت: «هو عدم الآخريَّة للوجود أو الثبوت فإن معنى العبارتين واحد. وأما الدليل على وجوب البقاء الله سبحانه فتقريره أنه لو جاز عليه العدم لاستحال أن يكون قديماً، لكنه سبحانه قد ثبت له القدم، فلا يجوز عليه العدم، فثبت وجوب البقاء له، أما الدليل على صحة الاستثنائية التي هي قولنا لكنه سبحانه قد ثبت له القدم» ، فهو ما قررناه في إثبات القدم الله سبحانه، وأما الدليل على صحة التّلازم في قولنا: «لو جاز عليه العدم لاستحال أن يكون قديما» فقد بينه المصنف آنفا بقوله : وكل ما جاز عليه العدم، عليه قطعا يستحيل القدم، قالوا: وقد أجمع العقلاء على هذه القضية. واعلم أن البقاء يطلق على أحد معنيين: أولهما ما قدمنا ذكرَه : وهو الذي يتصف الله تعالى به ويجب ثبوته له سبحانه. وثانيهما: «استمرار الوجود زمانين فصاعدا » ، وهذا المعنى مستحيل على الله تعالى، وهو الذي يراد عند وصف الحوادث بالبقاء، وإنما كان هذا المعنى مستحيلا على الله تعالى ؛ لأن الزمان عبارة عن حركة الفلك أو عبارة عن: مقارنة متجدد موهوم لمتجدد معلوم إزالة للإيهام وخذ مثالاً يوضّح لك هذا المعنى: إذا قلت: آتيك طلوع الشمس»، فالزمان هو مقارنة الإتيان وهو أمر متجدد موهوم لطلوع الشَّمس وهو أمر متجدد معلوم، ولا شكّ أنَّ كلَّا من حركة الفلك والمقارنة المذكورة حادث، ولا يقترن بالحادث إلَّا الحادثُ، وقد ثبت أنه تعالى قديم محي.
From [2 - al-Baqa'] (Thus) i.e.: like the necessity of existence and eternity for Him the Exalted (al-Baqa') is the second of the negative attributes, and its meaning: the impossibility of non-existence attaching to His existence; because what is established as eternal, its non-existence is impossible. And he described al-baqa' by his saying: (it is not mixed) i.e.: it does not intermix (with non-existence) nor does it attach to it; to guard against al-baqa' in the sense of the coexistence of the continuation of existence for two times or more, due to its impossibility for Him the Exalted in this sense; because of the impossibility of time entering into His existence the Exalted and all His attributes. And there has occurred among the scholars a disagreement concerning the meaning of al-baqa' like the disagreement that occurred among them concerning the meaning of eternity, and this disagreement is based on another disagreement whose summary is: Is al-baqa' a negative attribute or is it a self attribute like existence? Or is it an attribute of meanings? So among the scholars are those who claimed that al-baqa' is a self attribute like existence and interpreted it as 'the continual existence in what does not cease,' i.e., in the future without end, and among those who held this are al-Qadi Abu Bakr, Imam al-Haramayn, al-Razi, and the Mu'tazila of Basra. And among them are those who claimed that it is an attribute of meanings, like knowledge and power, and interpreted it as 'an attribute subsisting in the most holy essence, having an existence additional to the existence of the essence,' and among those who held this are Shaykh Abu al-Hasan and the Mu'tazila of Baghdad, and these two opinions are weak, and the correct view is that al-baqa' is a negative attribute, and its meaning is the negation of subsequent non-existence after existence or subsistence, and if you wish you could say: 'it is the non-existence of finality for existence or subsistence,' for the meaning of the two expressions is one. As for the proof of the necessity of al-baqa' for Allah the Glorious, its formulation is that if non-existence were possible for Him, it would be impossible for Him to be eternal, but He the Glorious has been established to have eternity, so non-existence is not possible for Him, thus the necessity of al-baqa' for Him is established. As for the proof of the validity of the conditional syllogism which is our saying 'but He the Glorious has been established to have eternity,' it is what we have explained in proving eternity for Allah the Glorious. And as for the proof of the validity of the implication in our saying 'if non-existence were possible for Him, it would be impossible for Him to be eternal,' the author has explained it previously by his saying: 'And everything upon which non-existence is possible, upon it eternity is absolutely impossible.' They said: 'The rational people have agreed on this proposition.' And know that al-baqa' is used in one of two senses: The first is what we have mentioned before: which is that with which Allah the Exalted is described and whose affirmation for Him the Glorious is necessary. And the second: 'the continuation of existence for two times or more,' and this sense is impossible for Allah the Exalted, and it is what is intended when describing contingent things with al-baqa'. And this sense is impossible for Allah the Exalted only because time is an expression for the motion of the celestial sphere or an expression for: the conjunction of an imagined renewing thing with a known renewing thing, to remove ambiguity. And take an example that clarifies this meaning for you: if you say: 'I come to you at the rising of the sun,' time is the conjunction of the coming, which is an imagined renewing thing, with the rising of the sun, which is a known renewing thing. And there is no doubt that each of the motion of the celestial sphere and the mentioned conjunction is contingent, and only the contingent accompanies the contingent, and it has been established that He the Exalted is eternal and living.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the divine attribute of al-baqa' (eternal perpetuity). It begins with a definition: al-baqa' is the second of the negative attributes, meaning the impossibility of non-existence attaching to His existence, because what is proven to be eternal (qadim) cannot cease to exist. The author then clarifies that the poem's phrase 'la yushabu bil-'adam' (it is not mixed with non-existence) is meant to distinguish this attribute from the ordinary sense of 'perpetuity' that implies duration over time, which is impossible for Allah because time itself is a created thing that cannot apply to the Creator. Next, he presents the scholarly disagreement about whether al-baqa' is a negative attribute (sifah salbiyyah), a self-attribute (sifah nafsiyyah) like existence, or an attribute of meanings (sifah ma'ani) like knowledge. He gives the two main opinions: that of al-Qadi Abu Bakr, Imam al-Haramayn, al-Razi, and the Basran Mu'tazila, who considered it a self-attribute; and that of Shaykh Abu al-Hasan and the Baghdad Mu'tazila, who considered it an attribute of meanings. Both opinions are deemed weak; the correct view is that it is a negative attribute, i.e., the negation of subsequent non-existence. The proof for its necessity is then given: if non-existence were possible for Allah, He would not be eternal, but He is eternal, so non-existence is impossible, therefore al-baqa' is necessary. The author further explains the evidence for the conditional statements in the proof, citing the earlier argument that anything subject to non-existence cannot be eternal, which is agreed upon by all rational people. Finally, he distinguishes two meanings of al-baqa': the divine sense (the necessary attribute of Allah) and the temporal sense (continued existence over two or more time units), which is impossible for Allah because time is contingent.

Key Terms
البقاء
الصفات السلبية
القدم
العدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Believing that al-Baqa' means Allah persists through time like created things.
Correction: Al-Baqa' is a negative attribute meaning non-existence is impossible, without reference to time.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what does the attribute al-Baqa' mean?
A) Allah continues to exist through all times.
B) It is impossible for Allah to cease to exist.
C) Allah's existence is mixed with non-existence.
D) Allah's existence is similar to created things.

Key Takeaway
Al-Baqa' is the negation of the possibility of non-existence for Allah, and it is not about duration in time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's existence is absolutely permanent, while everything else will inevitably cease, where are you placing your ultimate security? What in your life are you treating as if it will last forever, and how does that need to change starting today?
?
The passage says al-Baqa' is not about duration in time. This means God's permanence is not like a very long life—it is a different kind of reality. How does that challenge the way you imagine God? Are you reducing Him to a bigger version of created things? What will you do to know Him as He truly is?
?
Al-Baqa' is a negative attribute that negates deficiency. What deficiency in your own soul—like doubt, pride, or attachment to the world—are you tolerating instead of actively negating? What specific step will you take this week to fight that deficiency, knowing that Allah alone is perfect and permanent?

Scholarly Views on the Nature of al-Baqa'
Sanusi presents the scholarly disagreement on the nature of al-Baqa' and gives the correct view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three main scholarly positions on whether al-Baqa' is a negative attribute, a self-attribute, or an attribute of meanings, and which one is correct.

Core Idea
The correct view: al-Baqa' is a negative attribute, not an additional entity.

After defining al-Baqa', Sanusi presents a significant disagreement among scholars. The question is whether al-Baqa' is merely the negation of non-existence (negative attribute), identical to existence (self-attribute), or an additional attribute subsisting in the essence (attribute of meanings). This lesson maps out these positions and identifies the correct one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Read the passage and list the three views: 1) self-attribute, 2) attribute of meanings, 3) negative attribute. Note the proponents of each.
2
Understand the arguments
For each view, notice how they define al-Baqa'. The self-attribute view says it is 'continual existence in the future'; the attribute of meanings says it is an additional quality; the negative view says it is simply the negation of subsequent non-existence.
3
See the author's verdict
The author declares the first two views weak and affirms the negative attribute view as the correct one. Why might the other views be problematic?
Consider the principle of divine simplicity – no multiplicity in attributes that are additional to essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من [٢ - البقاء] (كَذَا ) أي : كوجُوبِ الوجُودِ والقِدَم له تعالى (بَقَاءُ) وهو الصفة الثانية الصَّفات السلبية، ومعناه: امتناع لحوق العدم لوجوده ؛ لأنَّ ما ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه. ووصَفَ البقاء بقوله: (لَا يُشَابُ) أي: لا يُخَالط (بِالْعَدَم) ولا يَلْحَقه ؛ ليحتَرِزَ به عن البقاء بمعنى مقارنة استمرار الوجود زمانين فصاعدا، لاستحالته عليه تعالى بهذا المعنى ؛ لامتناع دخول الزمان في وجوده تعالى وسائر صفاته. وقد جرى بين العلماء خلاف في معنى البقاء كالخلاف الجاري بينهم في معنى القدم، وهذا الخلاف مبني على خلاف آخر حاصله: هل البقاء صفة سلبية أم هو صفة نفسية كالوجود ؟ أم هو صفة من صفات المعاني ؟ فمن العلماء من زعم أن البقاء صفة نفسية كالوجود وفسره بأنه: «الوجود المستمر فيما لا يزال» ، أي : في المستقبل إلى غير نهاية، وممن ذهب إلى هذا القاضي أبوبكر، وإمام الحرمين، والرازي، ومعتزلة البصرة. ومنهم من زعم أنه صفة من صفات المعاني، كالعلم، والقدرة، وفسره: «بأنه صفة قائمة بالذات الأقدس، لها وجود زائد على وجود الذات»، وممن ذهب إلى هذا الشيخ أبو الحسن، ومعتزلة بغداد، وهذان الرأيان ضعيفان، والراجح أن البقاء : صفة سلبية، وأن معناه : نفي العدم اللاحق بعد الوجود أو الثبوت» وإن شئت قلت: «هو عدم الآخريَّة للوجود أو الثبوت فإن معنى العبارتين واحد. وأما الدليل على وجوب البقاء الله سبحانه فتقريره أنه لو جاز عليه العدم لاستحال أن يكون قديماً، لكنه سبحانه قد ثبت له القدم، فلا يجوز عليه العدم، فثبت وجوب البقاء له، أما الدليل على صحة الاستثنائية التي هي قولنا لكنه سبحانه قد ثبت له القدم» ، فهو ما قررناه في إثبات القدم الله سبحانه، وأما الدليل على صحة التّلازم في قولنا: «لو جاز عليه العدم لاستحال أن يكون قديما» فقد بينه المصنف آنفا بقوله : وكل ما جاز عليه العدم، عليه قطعا يستحيل القدم، قالوا: وقد أجمع العقلاء على هذه القضية. واعلم أن البقاء يطلق على أحد معنيين: أولهما ما قدمنا ذكرَه : وهو الذي يتصف الله تعالى به ويجب ثبوته له سبحانه. وثانيهما: «استمرار الوجود زمانين فصاعدا » ، وهذا المعنى مستحيل على الله تعالى، وهو الذي يراد عند وصف الحوادث بالبقاء، وإنما كان هذا المعنى مستحيلا على الله تعالى ؛ لأن الزمان عبارة عن حركة الفلك أو عبارة عن: مقارنة متجدد موهوم لمتجدد معلوم إزالة للإيهام وخذ يقترن بالحادث إلَّا الحادثُ، وقد ثبت أنه تعالى قديم محي.
From [2 - al-Baqa'] (Thus) i.e.: like the necessity of existence and eternity for Him the Exalted (al-Baqa') is the second of the negative attributes, and its meaning: the impossibility of non-existence attaching to His existence; because what is established as eternal, its non-existence is impossible. How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

Proof of the Necessity of al-Baqa'
Sanusi presents the logical proof for the necessity of al-Baqa' for Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof for the necessity of al-Baqa' for Allah, based on the impossibility of non-existence for the Eternal.

Core Idea
If non-existence were possible, Allah would not be eternal; but He is, so it is impossible.

Having established the correct definition of al-Baqa', Sanusi now provides a formal proof for its necessity. The proof is a conditional syllogism: if non-existence were possible, then eternity would be impossible; but eternity is established, so non-existence is impossible. This lesson unpacks the proof and its supporting arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof structure
Notice the logical form: 'if... then... but... so...' Identify the conditional statement and the exception.
This is a classic qiyas istithna'i (conditional syllogism).
2
Understand the premise
The conditional premise: 'if non-existence were possible for Him, it would be impossible for Him to be eternal.' The author explains that this premise is agreed upon by all rational people.
3
Connect to earlier proof
The author references the earlier proof for eternity (qidam) to support the minor premise that Allah is eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And among them are those who claimed that it is an attribute of meanings, like knowledge and power, and interpreted it as 'an attribute subsisting in the most holy essence, having an existence additional to the existence of the essence,' and among those who held this are Shaykh Abu al-Hasan and the Mu'tazila of Baghdad, and these two opinions are weak, and the correct view is that al-baqa' is a negative attribute, and its meaning is the negation of subsequent non-existence after existence or subsistence, and if you wish you could say: 'it is the non-existence of finality for existence or subsistence,' for the meaning of the two expressions is one. As for the proof of the necessity of al-baqa' for Allah the Glorious, its formulation is that if non-existence were possible for Him, it would be impossible for Him to be eternal, but He the Glorious has been established to have eternity, so non-existence is not possible for Him, thus the necessity of al-baqa' for Him is established. As for the proof of the validity of the conditional syllogism which is our saying 'but He the Glorious has been established to have eternity,' it is what we have explained in proving eternity for Allah the Glorious. And as for the proof of the validity of the implication in our saying 'if non-existence were possible for Him, it would be impossible for Him to be eternal,' the author has explained it previously by his saying: 'And everything upon which non-existence is possible, upon it eternity is absolutely impossible.' They said: 'The rational people have agreed on this proposition.' And know that al-baqa' is used in one of two senses: The first is what we have mentioned before: which is that with which Allah the Exalted is described and whose affirmation for Him the Glorious is necessary. And the second: 'the continuation of existence for two times or more,' and this sense is impossible for Allah the Exalted, and it is what is intended when describing contingent things with al-baqa'. And this sense is impossible for Allah the Exalted only because time is an expression for the motion of the celestial sphere or an expression for: the conjunction of an imagined renewing thing with a known renewing thing, to remove ambiguity. And take an example that clarifies this meaning for you: if you say: 'I come to you at the rising of the sun,' time is the conjunction of the coming, which is an imagined renewing thing, with the rising of the sun, which is a known renewing thing. And there is no doubt that each of the motion of the celestial sphere and the mentioned conjunction is contingent, and only the contingent accompanies the contingent, and it has been established that He the Exalted is eternal and living.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the divine attribute of al-baqa' (eternal perpetuity). It begins with a definition: al-baqa' is the second of the negative attributes, meaning the impossibility of non-existence attaching to His existence, because what is proven to be eternal (qadim) cannot cease to exist. The author then clarifies that the poem's phrase 'la yushabu bil-'adam' (it is not mixed with non-existence) is meant to distinguish this attribute from the ordinary sense of 'perpetuity' that implies duration over time, which is impossible for Allah because time itself is a created thing that cannot apply to the Creator. Next, he presents the scholarly disagreement about whether al-baqa' is a negative attribute (sifah salbiyyah), a self-attribute (sifah nafsiyyah) like existence, or an attribute of meanings (sifah ma'ani) like knowledge. He gives the two main opinions: that of al-Qadi Abu Bakr, Imam al-Haramayn, al-Razi, and the Basran Mu'tazila, who considered it a self-attribute; and that of Shaykh Abu al-Hasan and the Baghdad Mu'tazila, who considered it an attribute of meanings. Both opinions are deemed weak; the correct view is that it is a negative attribute, i.e., the negation of subsequent non-existence. The proof for its necessity is then given: if non-existence were possible for Allah, He would not be eternal, but He is eternal, so non-existence is impossible, therefore al-baqa' is necessary. The author further explains the evidence for the conditional statements in the proof, citing the earlier argument that anything subject to non-existence cannot be eternal, which is agreed upon by all rational people. Finally, he distinguishes two meanings of al-baqa': the divine sense (the necessary attribute of Allah) and the temporal sense (continued existence over two or more time units), which is impossible for Allah because time is contingent.

Key Terms

Misconception: Thinking that the proof relies on scripture rather than reason.
Correction: The proof is purely rational, based on the logical principle that what can cease cannot be eternal.

C) Non-existence is impossible for Allah.

Key Takeaway
The necessity of al-Baqa' is proven rationally: since Allah is eternal, non-existence is impossible.

The Two Meanings of al-Baqa'
Sanusi distinguishes two meanings of al-Baqa' and explains the impossibility of the temporal sense for Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between the divine meaning of al-Baqa' (negation of non-existence) and the temporal meaning (continuation through time), and why the latter is impossible for Allah.

Core Idea
Al-Baqa' for Allah is not temporal; time is a creature and cannot apply to the Creator.

Sanusi concludes his treatment of al-Baqa' by highlighting a crucial distinction. The word 'baqa' can be used in two very different senses: one fitting for Allah (negation of non-existence) and another that implies duration over time, which is impossible for the Eternal. He explains why time cannot apply to Allah by defining time itself as a contingent measurement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two meanings
Read the passage and list the two meanings: the divine (negation of subsequent non-existence) and the temporal (continuation over two or more times).
2
Understand why temporal is impossible
The author says time is the motion of the sphere or the conjunction of imagined and known renewing things. Both are contingent and cannot be attributed to Allah.
3
See the example
The example of 'I come to you at sunrise' illustrates how time is a relation between two contingent events. Allah is beyond such relations.

صفاته. وقد جرى بين العلماء خلاف في معنى البقاء كالخلاف الجاري بينهم في معنى القدم، وهذا الخلاف مبني على خلاف آخر حاصله: هل البقاء صفة سلبية أم هو صفة نفسية كالوجود ؟ أم هو صفة من صفات المعاني ؟ فمن جاز عليه العدم لاستحال أن يكون قديماً، لكنه سبحانه قد ثبت له القدم، فلا يجوز عليه العدم، فثبت وجوب البقاء له، أما الدليل على صحة الاستثنائية التي هي قولنا لكنه سبحانه قد ثبت له القدم» ، فهو ما قررناه في إثبات القدم الله سبحانه، وأما الدليل على صحة التّلازم في قولنا: «لو جاز عليه العدم لاستحال أن يكون قديما» فقد بينه المصنف آنفا بقوله : وكل ما جاز عليه العدم، عليه قطعا يستحيل القدم، قالوا: وقد أجمع العقلاء على هذه القضية. واعلم أن البقاء يطلق على أحد معنيين: أولهما ما قدمنا ذكرَه : وهو الذي يتصف الله تعالى به ويجب ثبوته له سبحانه. وثانيهما: «استمرار الوجود زمانين فصاعدا » ، وهذا المعنى مستحيل From [2 - al-Baqa'] (Thus) i.e.: like the necessity of existence and eternity for Him the Exalted (al-Baqa') is the second of the negative attributes, and its meaning: the impossibility of non-existence attaching to His existence; because what is established as eternal, its non-existence is impossible.
